Another student correctly argued that it was narrowing the scope too much, ignoring that a university classroom is filled with people who have multiple different goals beyond just finding a corporate job. I clarified that Karishma's group didn't necessarily do anything wrong—I wasn't trying to nail them down. Having a narrow question is fine *if* you actually consulted with the decision-maker first. If you had gone to Professor Tan and asked, "What is your main intention?" and he replied, "My students complain they aren't getting placed, I want to fix that for the future," then their narrow problem statement would be perfectly valid. However, if they just assumed that was the goal without asking, that is problematic. As analysts, you must interface with your decision-maker first to understand what they truly want. If you just take a broad prompt, assume a narrow goal, and run with it, you are doing it wrong.

    Karishma then elaborated that they realized the scope was too narrow, so they looked at the "NUS 120" vision documents to see what the university was already planning for the next 5 to 10 years. They saw alignments with national goals like sustainability, health, innovation, and the Smart Nation initiative. They dug deeper into NUS's specific focus on research centers and entrepreneurship hubs. This led them to reframe their question from just "picking up job skills" to preparing students for a rapidly evolving, diverse landscape. I praised this pivot, noting that this is exactly how the intelligence process should organically evolve. Karishma concluded that based on these aligned visions, they mapped out different scenarios—one focused purely on jobs, another heavily on entrepreneurship backed by NUS's new venture funding—and decided they would gather data specifically aligned with those diverging scenarios.

    Karishma展示了她所在小组的方法，说他们主要关注帮助学生更快地掌握就业市场所需的技能。他们的依据是调查显示，本科生和研究生目前最关心的是找工作。我打断了她并向全班提问。她所在小组的假设是，2032年教室的首要目标是帮助学生在就业市场上处于更有利的位置。我问全班：“你们中有多少人喜欢这种设定一个清晰、狭窄的框架问题的方法？”然后我又问：“你们中有多少人不喜欢，为什么？”一位学生指出，他们不能完全确定那个特定的问题——当前的就业焦虑——在2032年是否仍然会是主要问题。另一位学生准确地指出，这把范围缩小得太多了，忽略了大学教室里充满了有着除了找公司工作之外多种不同目标的人。我澄清说，Karishma的小组未必做错了什么——我不是想为难他们。*如果*你实际上先咨询了决策者，那么有一个狭窄的问题是没问题的。如果你去问陈教授：“你的主要意图是什么？”他回答说：“我的学生抱怨他们找不到工作，我想在未来解决这个问题，”那么他们狭窄的问题陈述就完全有效了。然而，如果他们不问就假设那是目标，那就有问题了。作为分析师，你必须首先与你的决策者沟通，以了解他们真正想要什么。如果你只是接受一个宽泛的提示，假设一个狭窄的目标，然后就照着做，那你就做错了。

    Karishma接着详细说明，他们意识到范围太窄了，所以他们查看了“NUS 120”愿景文件，看看大学已经为未来5到10年规划了什么。他们看到了与可持续发展、健康、创新和智慧国（Smart Nation）倡议等国家目标的契合。他们深入研究了新加坡国立大学对研究中心和创业中心的具体关注。这促使他们重新构建了他们的问题，从仅仅“掌握工作技能”转变为让学生为快速发展、多样化的环境做好准备。我赞扬了这种转变，指出这正是情报过程应该如何有机发展的。Karishma总结说，基于这些一致的愿景，他们描绘了不同的情景——一个纯粹关注就业，另一个在新加坡国立大学新的风险投资支持下重点关注创业——并决定他们将专门收集与这些不同情景相一致的数据。

  - [19:25:25 - 19:30:10] **Expanding the Scope of Data Collection**

    I then pushed Karishma's group further on exactly *how* and from *whom* they would collect this data. She suggested using surveys to ask the current student population and faculty. I challenged this immediately: "Are current students really the right focus group?" Another student interjected, correctly pointing out that current students are anchored in the present, not the future. I agreed, explaining that while a focus group is the right methodology, you need to involve futuristic thinkers. You should be talking to future students currently in secondary schools, or consulting with Ministry of Education (MOE) policymakers. You must even look into the evolving learning psychology of the next generation, because how you learn today is completely different from how my young son learns now. If Professor Tan just blasts out a mandatory survey to current NUS students, he is just collecting hindsight. As an intelligence analyst, your job is to find the data he cannot easily access himself.

    I shared a real example: a couple of years ago, when Professor Tan was pondering similar futuristic questions, he was closely monitoring a Chinese company called Ping An. He was deeply impressed by how rapidly they were evolving across the finance and medical sectors, and he wanted NUS to match that agility. That is the level at which decision-makers operate—they are looking at cross-industry transformations. Therefore, you cannot confine your intelligence gathering solely to the education sector. I asked the class: "Can you think of entities completely outside of the traditional education sector that are currently threatening to dramatically disrupt it?" A student correctly identified tech companies. Exactly. Massive tech giants are starting their own rigorous training programs and issuing their own recognized certifications. Today's youth are already asking, "Why should I spend years at a university and struggle to find a job when I can just get trained directly by Google or Microsoft and get absorbed into their workforce immediately?" If tech giants aggressively enter the education space, what will NUS or NTU do? Professor Tan desperately needs to think about that, especially regarding our Master's programs. Intelligence gathering is not just about researching classroom infrastructure or hiring better teachers; it is about analyzing broader industry threats. Should Professor Tan proactively collaborate with these tech giants? That is vital intelligence. As an intelligence expert, your absolute first duty is to expose your decision-maker to all potential external threats and radical opportunities so they are prepared.

    然后我进一步追问Karishma的小组，他们究竟将*如何*以及从*谁*那里收集这些数据。她建议使用调查问卷来询问在校学生和教职员工。我立刻对这一点提出了质疑：“现在的学生真的是合适的焦点小组吗？”另一名学生插话，准确地指出现在的学生立足于现在，而不是未来。我表示同意，并解释说，虽然焦点小组是正确的方法，但你需要让具有未来思维的人参与进来。你应该与目前在中学就读的未来学生交谈，或者咨询教育部（MOE）的政策制定者。你甚至必须研究下一代不断演变的学习心理学，因为你们现在的学习方式与我年幼的儿子现在的学习方式完全不同。如果陈教授只是向当前的新加坡国立大学学生强制发送一份调查问卷，他收集到的只是事后诸葛亮的数据。作为一名情报分析师，你的工作是找到他自己无法轻易获取的数据。

    我分享了一个真实的例子：几年前，当陈教授在思考类似的未来问题时，他正在密切关注一家名为中国平安的中国公司。他对他们跨越金融和医疗领域的快速发展印象深刻，他希望新加坡国立大学也能具备同样的敏捷性。这就是决策者运作的层面——他们着眼于跨行业的转型。因此，你不能将情报收集仅仅局限于教育部门。我问全班同学：“你们能想到完全在传统教育部门之外，目前正威胁要大幅颠覆它的实体吗？”一名学生准确地指出了科技公司。完全正确。大型科技巨头正在开展自己严格的培训计划，并颁发自己受认可的证书。今天的年轻人已经在问：“如果我能直接接受谷歌或微软的培训，并立即加入他们的员工队伍，为什么我还要在大学里耗费数年，然后还要努力找工作呢？”如果科技巨头大举进入教育领域，新加坡国立大学或南洋理工大学会怎么做？陈教授迫切需要考虑这一点，尤其是关于我们的硕士项目。情报收集不仅仅是研究教室的基础设施或聘请更好的老师；它是关于分析更广泛的行业威胁。陈教授应该主动与这些科技巨头合作吗？这是至关重要的情报。作为一名情报专家，你的首要职责是向你的决策者揭示所有潜在的外部威胁和激进的机会，让他们做好准备。

  - [19:30:10 - 19:36:50] **Critique of Group 2: Confusing Hindsight with Foresight**

    Next, Zuhair and Jared's group presented. Zuhair explained that they tried to apply the "Hindsight, Insight, Foresight" strategy. For hindsight, they tracked the evolution of information sharing—from chalkboards, to presentations, to the rapid digitalization during COVID-19, leading to the current hybrid model where documents are shared before class even begins. Their insight was that since information is now easily accessible, the current challenge is fostering actual classroom engagement rather than mere information transfer. Jared then extrapolated this into the future, suggesting specific technological solutions like interactive desk buttons, learning from how parliaments or government sectors operate. He also heavily emphasized implementing VR headsets, suggesting students could visualize complex environments or run dangerous chemistry experiments virtually without risk, keeping them highly engaged. Finally, he briefly mentioned a more radical idea: using brainwave monitoring to allow students to interact with whiteboards mentally.

    I gave them my quick critique: While the thought process was good, their initial recommendations were almost entirely based on hindsight and present-day reality, not true foresight. For instance, I pointed out that the VR chemistry lab idea they presented as a futuristic solution *already exists* right here at NUS. The Chemical Engineering department currently uses VR because they cannot safely take students to real chemical plants. It is already implemented. This highlights a critical lesson from Carlson’s framework regarding the "Power Zone": many times, in a massive organization, information is so siloed that you don't even know what your own company is already doing. You might pitch a "futuristic" idea that a different department deployed two years ago! That is why thoroughly understanding your present Power Zone is the mandatory first step. I clarified that I wasn't shooting them down, but emphasizing that they must push past existing tech.

    I did, however, praise Jared's mention of brainwave monitoring, noting that this is genuinely futuristic. I reminded the class of a video I showed in MT5007 about what is currently happening in China, where students wear headbands that use AI to monitor their brainwaves to see if they are focusing, sending real-time data to the teacher. This opens up entirely new intelligence avenues: while the technology exists, the global ethical backlash is massive. People argue it is exploitative and unethical. As an intelligence officer, if you present this brainwave technology to Professor Tan as a potential future classroom tool, you absolutely must also provide the intelligence regarding the severe ethical pitfalls and regulatory risks associated with it.

    接下来是Zuhair和Jared的小组展示。Zuhair解释说，他们试图应用“后见、洞察、预见”的策略。在回顾过去时，他们追踪了信息共享的演变——从黑板到演示文稿，再到新冠疫情期间的快速数字化，最终演变成目前的混合模式，即在上课前就共享文件。他们的洞察是，既然现在信息很容易获取，当前的挑战是促进实际的课堂参与，而不仅仅是信息传递。Jared随后将其推断到未来，提出了一些具体的技术解决方案，例如交互式桌面按钮，借鉴议会或政府部门的运作方式。他还非常强调应用VR头显，建议学生可以直观地看到复杂的环境，或者在没有风险的情况下虚拟地进行危险的化学实验，让他们保持高度的参与度。最后，他简要地提到了一个更激进的想法：使用脑电波监测让学生在精神上与白板互动。

    我给出了我的快速点评：虽然思维过程很好，但他们最初的建议几乎完全基于后见之明和现状，而不是真正的预见。例如，我指出他们作为未来解决方案提出的VR化学实验室在新加坡国立大学“已经存在”了。化学工程系目前正在使用VR，因为他们无法安全地带学生去真正的化工厂。它已经投入使用了。这突出了Carlson框架中关于“实力区”的一个关键教训：很多时候，在一个庞大的组织中，信息是如此孤立，以至于你甚至不知道你自己的公司已经在做什么。你可能会推销一个其他部门两年前就已经部署的“未来”想法！这就是为什么彻底了解你目前的实力区是强制性的第一步。我澄清说我不是在打击他们，而是在强调他们必须超越现有的技术。

    不过，我赞扬了Jared提到的脑电波监测，指出这确实具有未来感。我提醒全班同学，我在MT5007课上放过一个关于中国目前正在发生的事情的视频，在那儿学生们戴着使用AI监测脑电波的发带，看看他们是否在专心，并将实时数据发送给老师。这开辟了全新的情报途径：虽然技术存在，但全球范围内的伦理反弹是巨大的。人们认为这是剥削和不道德的。作为一名情报官员，如果你向陈教授展示这种脑电波技术作为潜在的未来课堂工具，你绝对必须同时提供关于其严重的伦理陷阱和相关监管风险的情报。

  - [19:36:50 - 19:41:35] **Synthesizing the Ideal Foresight Process**

    Finally, a last group shared a very streamlined approach: they stated they would quickly secure experienced teachers, immediately research future trends, and then map out different scenarios to enhance current strengths against other countries. I praised this because it perfectly captured the *process* flow I was looking for. I summarized the ideal sequence for the class: First, as the intelligence officer, you sit down with Professor Tan to aggressively narrow down the true scope and intent of his question. Second, you assemble a highly diverse focus group workshop. Crucially, as Carlson’s article demands, this group must include people from entirely different business areas—not just teachers and students, but IT infrastructure experts, campus security, and people from other faculties. Why? Because if you propose a VR idea, the chemical engineering guy will immediately tell you they already did it. If you propose AI brainwaves, the computer science expert will immediately brief you on the ethical disaster happening in China. Bringing these diverse stakeholders together immediately pools fractured information and prevents redundant work.

    After that initial workshop, you assign these diverse stakeholders specific, targeted areas to research. They go out, gather fresh external data, and return for the second workshop. Here, they present their trend analysis. Based on this rich data, you paint three or four drastically different potential scenarios for the 2032 classroom. You lay these scenarios in front of Professor Tan. He does not decide, "This is the single future we are building." Instead, he decides how to spread his investments to be safe. Even knowing the ethical risks, he might invest heavily in brainwave tech if he believes distraction is an existential threat to learning. Or, he might bet heavily on holographic tech to pull in global industry experts seamlessly. He places strategic bets on the directions that seem most worthwhile. Your job is to facilitate the data collection, engage the right minds, and ensure the decision-maker is completely synergistic with the intelligence process. Another student noted this sounds very similar to general problem-solving. I agreed it shares DNA with problem-solving—which can range from tactical to operational—but foresighting is uniquely strategic and entirely focused on navigating deep future uncertainty.

    最后，最后一个小组分享了一个非常精简的方法：他们表示，他们将迅速锁定有经验的教师，立即研究未来趋势，然后描绘不同的情景，以增强相对于其他国家的现有优势。我赞扬了这一点，因为它完美地抓住了我正在寻找的“过程”流程。我为全班总结了理想的顺序：首先，作为情报官员，你坐下来与陈教授深入探讨，以极大地缩小他问题的真实范围和意图。其次，你召集一个高度多样化的焦点小组研讨会。至关重要的是，正如Carlson的文章所要求的那样，这个小组必须包括来自完全不同业务领域的人——不仅仅是老师和学生，还包括IT基础设施专家、校园安保人员以及来自其他院系的人员。为什么？因为如果你提出一个VR的想法，化学工程的人会立刻告诉你他们已经这么做了。如果你提出AI脑电波，计算机科学专家会立刻向你简要介绍中国正在发生的伦理灾难。将这些不同的利益相关者聚集在一起，可以立即汇集零碎的信息，并防止重复工作。

    在那次初步研讨会之后，你分配给这些不同的利益相关者具体的、有针对性的领域进行研究。他们出去收集新鲜的外部数据，然后回来参加第二次研讨会。在这里，他们展示他们的趋势分析。基于这些丰富的数据，你为2032年的教室描绘了三到四个截然不同的潜在情景。你把这些情景摆在陈教授面前。他并不是决定：“这就是我们将要构建的唯一未来。”相反，他决定如何分散投资以确保安全。即使知道伦理风险，如果他认为分心是对学习的生存威胁，他也可能会在脑电波技术上投入巨资。或者，他可能会在全息技术上下重注，以无缝地引进全球行业专家。他在看起来最有价值的方向上进行战略押注。你的工作是促进数据收集，让合适的人才参与进来，并确保决策者与情报过程完全协同。另一名学生指出这听起来非常类似于一般的问题解决。我同意它与解决问题（可以从战术层面到运营层面）有共同点，但预见具有独特的战略性，并且完全专注于驾驭深远的未来不确定性。

  - [19:41:35 - 19:50:31] **Mentimeter Quiz and the Agile Nature of Roadmaps**

    Returning to the lecture notes, I pulled up a quick Mentimeter quiz to test their understanding of the Lockwood Carlson article and to demonstrate the interactive format of future classes. The first question asked if technology foresight identifies threats, opportunities, or both. The class easily agreed it was both, which I had verbally covered earlier. The next question asked if technology foresight ignores the present to look only at the future. I emphatically reminded them that you absolutely cannot ignore the present. True foresighting demands that you know exactly where your "Power Zone" currently is so you can map the path from today to those potential futures five or ten years away.

    The third question was critical: Is technology foresight a one-time activity, an ongoing process, or both? I was very happy to see that no one answered "one-time activity." However, I had to deliberately pause and explain the harsh reality. In an ideal world, it is an ongoing process. But practically, many real-world organizations treat it as a one-off event. They lack the resources, culture, or visionary leadership to sustain it, so they run one workshop, build a rigid roadmap, and treat it like a Bible. I asked the class if they knew what a "roadmap" was, explaining it is basically charting where you are, where you want to go, and the steps to get there. If a company treats a roadmap as a rigid, one-time document, they are guaranteed to fail. A roadmap must be incredibly agile. I used a sailing analogy: If you are the captain of a ship with many passengers, you know your final destination. But can you stubbornly plot one single, unchangeable route? Absolutely not. You have to constantly adjust for changing winds, dangerous tides, and unpredictable currents. Foresighting is not about blindly following a Bible; it is about knowing how to dynamically navigate your investments as new scenarios arise, ensuring you aren't trapped in a dead-end technology. The article technically answers "both," because while it *should* be ongoing, many poorly resourced SMEs can only afford to do it once.

    We then briefly touched on the scope of foresighting, agreeing it happens at every level—from individual career planning to massive global initiatives like multi-nation pacts tackling CO2 emissions. Finally, I asked if foresighting must strictly be triggered top-down by management. A student practically noted that top-down is required to actually secure funding and buy-in. Another student countered that ideally, it should be bottom-up, triggered by anyone who spots a critical trend. I explained that while many hierarchical companies force a top-down approach, the most innovative organizations cultivate a bottom-up culture where ground-level intelligence flows upward. We will explore the friction between hierarchical and intelligent organizations in Week 4.

    回到讲义，我调出了一个简短的Mentimeter测验，以测试他们对Lockwood Carlson文章的理解，并展示未来课程的互动形式。第一个问题问技术预见是识别威胁、机会，还是两者兼有。全班很容易地达成共识，认为是两者兼有，我早先已经口头讲过了。下一个问题问技术预见是否忽略现在只看未来。我着重提醒他们，你绝对不能忽略现在。真正的预见要求你确切地知道你目前的“实力区”在哪里，这样你才能描绘出从今天到五年或十年后那些潜在未来的路径。

    第三个问题很关键：技术预见是一次性活动、持续的过程，还是两者兼有？我很高兴看到没有人回答“一次性活动”。然而，我不得不刻意停顿下来，解释残酷的现实。在一个理想的世界里，它是一个持续的过程。但在现实中，许多现实世界的组织把它当作一次性的事件来对待。他们缺乏资源、文化或有远见的领导力来维持它，所以他们举办一次研讨会，制定一个僵化的路线图，然后把它当成圣经。我问全班同学是否知道什么是“路线图（roadmap）”，并解释说这基本上就是规划你现在在哪里、你想去哪里以及到达那里的步骤。如果一家公司把路线图当作一份僵化的、一次性的文件，他们注定会失败。路线图必须极其敏捷。我用航海做了一个比喻：如果你是一艘载有许多乘客的船的船长，你知道你的最终目的地。但你能固执地规划出一条单一的、不可改变的路线吗？绝对不能。你必须根据不断变化的风向、危险的潮汐和不可预测的洋流不断进行调整。预见不是盲目地遵循圣经；它是关于知道随着新情况的出现，如何动态地引导你的投资，确保你不会陷入技术的死胡同。这篇文章在技术上回答了“两者兼有”，因为虽然它“应该”是持续的，但许多资源匮乏的中小企业只能负担得起做一次。

    然后我们简要地触及了预见的范围，同意它发生在每一个层面——从个人职业规划到像应对二氧化碳排放的多国协议这样庞大的全球倡议。最后，我问预见是否必须严格由管理层自上而下地触发。一名学生从实际出发指出，自上而下是实际获得资金和支持所必需的。另一名学生反驳说，理想情况下，它应该是自下而上的，由任何发现关键趋势的人触发。我解释说，虽然许多等级森严的公司强制采用自上而下的方法，但最具创新性的组织会培养一种自下而上的文化，让基层的智慧向上流动。我们将在第四周探讨等级森严的组织与智能型组织之间的摩擦。

  - [19:50:31 - 19:56:49] **The Three Strategic Decisions of Foresighting**

    I wrapped up the discussion on Carlson's framework by explicitly detailing the three final strategic decisions an organization must make after completing the foresighting process. First, you must decide what aspects of your Power Zone to **Enhance**. Using myself as an example, my Power Zone is teaching, research, and service. If my gathered intelligence indicates that AI is fully automating traditional lectures, then traditional teaching might be a dead end. Therefore, I must intentionally choose to enhance my research skills, specifically integrating AI into my portfolio, to survive. However, if the data shows that students still deeply crave human empathy that AI cannot provide, then I must double down and enhance my interpersonal teaching skills.

    Second, you decide what to **Extend**. If my current research does not involve Machine Learning, but the industry is undeniably moving that way, I must extend my existing research capabilities to include ML techniques, stretching my Power Zone into adjacent territory.

    Third, you must identify **New Opportunities** to exploit. If tech companies are bypassing universities and creating their own private educational ecosystems, I have to ask myself: Should I remain exclusively loyal to NUS, or should I take a massive risk and start heavily collaborating with corporate training centers? Embracing new opportunities often requires risking your current stability, much like a metallurgy company abandoning core products to invest in untested alloys, or abandoning solar to pivot to geothermal. The entire purpose of the power zone mapping, the workshops, and the data gathering is to formulate a strategy that answers these three exact questions, thereby mitigating fatal threats and exploiting lucrative new frontiers. I skipped over the complex, centroid-based mathematical slides detailing how to plot these zones, reminding the students not to get lost in the micro-techniques, as different companies use drastically different plotting methods. The overarching process is what truly matters.

    我通过明确详细地说明一个组织在完成预见过程后必须做出的三个最终战略决策，结束了对Carlson框架的讨论。首先，你必须决定**增强（Enhance）**你实力区的哪些方面。以我自己为例，我的实力区是教学、研究和服务。如果我收集到的情报表明，人工智能正在将传统讲座完全自动化，那么传统教学可能是一条死胡同。因此，我必须刻意选择提高我的研究技能，特别是将AI整合到我的投资组合中，以求生存。然而，如果数据显示学生仍然深深渴望AI无法提供的人类同理心，那么我必须加倍努力并提高我的人际教学技能。

    其次，你决定**扩展（Extend）**什么。如果我目前的研究不涉及机器学习，但毫无疑问行业正在朝着这个方向发展，我必须扩展我现有的研究能力以包括ML技术，将我的实力区延伸到相邻的领域。

    第三，你必须找出可以利用的**新机会（New Opportunities）**。如果科技公司绕过大学，建立自己的私人教育生态系统，我不得不问自己：我应该继续完全忠诚于新加坡国立大学，还是应该冒着巨大的风险开始与企业培训中心大力合作？拥抱新机会通常需要拿你目前的稳定性冒险，就像一家冶金公司放弃核心产品去投资未经测试的合金，或者放弃太阳能转向地热能一样。绘制实力区图、举办研讨会和收集数据的全部目的，就是制定一个准确回答这三个问题的战略，从而减轻致命威胁并利用利润丰厚的新领域。我跳过了详细说明如何绘制这些区域的、复杂的、基于质心的数学幻灯片，提醒学生们不要迷失在微观技术中，因为不同的公司使用的绘制方法截然不同。真正重要的是总体的过程。

  - [19:56:49 - 20:02:20] **Terminology: Scouting, Monitoring, and the Evolution to Foresight**

    I moved on to clarify some specific industry terminology. While "intelligence" might be a broad term, you must understand activities like Technology Scouting and Technology Monitoring. I asked the class to define technology scouting. Big companies do this constantly: they aggressively survey the landscape to find startup companies or university research labs developing top-notch, disruptive technologies, and they simply buy them out or absorb their research. Technology monitoring, on the other hand, is highly targeted. For instance, anyone in the educational technology sector who is serious about AI will obsessively monitor Georgia Tech. Why? Because the professors there are famous for developing cutting-edge AI teaching tools and secretly deploying them in their own classrooms long before they ever hit the commercial market. As an intelligence specialist, knowing to monitor Georgia Tech gives your decision-maker a massive competitive advantage.

    I then explained the historical evolution from simple forecasting to complex foresighting. In the past, when supply chains were simple and localized, forecasting one or two steps ahead based on historical data was sufficient. But today, the environment is violently dynamic. I shared an anecdote about a colleague, Bert, who ran a massive foresighting project for the company that makes Oreo cookies. When the Ukraine-Russia war broke out, a critical, obscure ingredient for Oreos that was sourced exclusively from that region suddenly vanished. A massive global brand was instantly paralyzed by a geopolitical conflict half a world away. They desperately had to foresee plant-based alternatives to keep production alive. This proved that intelligence cannot be narrow-minded. You cannot just look at your immediate technology; you must analyze the macro socio-economic and geopolitical environment over a long horizon. That realization is why modern organizations abandoned rigid forecasting and embraced fluid foresighting.

    我接着澄清了一些具体的行业术语。虽然“情报”可能是一个宽泛的术语，但你必须了解技术搜寻（Technology Scouting）和技术监控（Technology Monitoring）等活动。我让全班同学定义技术搜寻。大公司经常这么做：他们积极地调查市场，寻找开发顶尖、颠覆性技术的初创公司或大学研究实验室，然后干脆将它们买断或吸收它们的研究成果。另一方面，技术监控则非常有针对性。例如，任何在教育技术领域认真对待AI的人都会痴迷地监控佐治亚理工学院（Georgia Tech）。为什么？因为那里的教授以开发尖端的人工智能教学工具而闻名，并且在它们进入商业市场之前很久，就秘密地将它们部署在自己的课堂上。作为一名情报专家，知道去监控佐治亚理工学院能给你的决策者带来巨大的竞争优势。

    然后我解释了从简单的预测到复杂的预见的历史演变。在过去，当供应链简单且本地化时，根据历史数据预测未来一两步就足够了。但今天，环境剧烈动荡。我分享了关于同事Bert的一件轶事，他为生产奥利奥（Oreo）饼干的公司进行了一个庞大的预见项目。当乌克兰-俄罗斯战争爆发时，一种专门从该地区采购的奥利奥关键、冷门原料突然断货。一个庞大的全球品牌瞬间被半个地球之外的地缘政治冲突所瘫痪。他们不得不拼命寻找基于植物的替代品来维持生产。这证明了情报不能目光短浅。你不能只盯着眼前的技术；你必须在一个较长的时间跨度内分析宏观的社会经济和地缘政治环境。这种认识正是现代组织放弃僵化的预测转而拥抱流动的预见的原因。

  - [20:02:20 - 20:07:27] **Module Roadmap and Group Project Details**

    Quickly covering the module structure: The first half is heavily theoretical—understanding what intelligence is and how it is structured. The second half is intensely hands-on, focusing on specific tools like the Delphi method, bibliometric analysis, scenario analysis, and roadmapping. I noted that I used to teach Patent Data Analytics within this module, but analyzing patents to find "white spaces" for R&D is such an incredibly vast ocean of knowledge that I actually spun it off into its own entirely separate module offered this semester. If you are serious about foresighting, those two modules go hand-in-hand. Because the second half is highly analytical and utilizes open-source software and Excel, I will provide the core instructional steps via pre-recorded videos. This allows the data experts in the class to skim rapidly, while beginners can pause and work step-by-step at their own pace. We have several guest lectures planned, including Seng Meng next week and Renee from France in Week 5. After the long Chinese New Year break, I will cover Knowledge Management. I initially planned to travel, but decided to stay and push through the material because the large class size means we desperately need two full weeks just for final presentations.

    Regarding those final group projects: You have two choices. The superior option is an open-ended project where you analyze the actual intelligence activities of a real company—for example, mapping out how SP Group dictates national energy intelligence, or how a specific startup navigates its space. If you lack industry access or work experience, you can use the fallback option provided in Canvas: a case study on "Straumann," a Swiss SME. Let me be brutally frank: groups that hustle to do an open-ended project on a real company will absolutely score higher than those who just present the pre-packaged Straumann case. Straumann is merely a hygiene factor for those with zero experience; do the open-ended project if you want top marks.

    快速介绍课程结构：前半部分侧重理论——了解什么是情报以及它是如何构建的。后半部分则是高强度的实践，重点介绍具体工具，如德尔菲法（Delphi method）、文献计量分析（bibliometric analysis）、情景分析（scenario analysis）和路线图制定（roadmapping）。我提到我以前在这门课中教授专利数据分析（Patent Data Analytics），但分析专利以寻找研发的“空白领域”是一个极其广阔的知识海洋，以至于我实际上把它剥离出来，作为本学期提供的一门完全独立的课程。如果你对预见很认真，这两门课是相辅相成的。因为后半部分分析性很强，并且使用开源软件和Excel，我将通过预先录制的视频提供核心的操作步骤。这使得班上的数据专家可以快速浏览，而初学者可以暂停并按照自己的节奏一步步地操作。我们计划了几次客座讲座，包括下周的Seng Meng和第五周来自法国的Renee。在漫长的农历新年假期之后，我将讲解知识管理。我最初计划去旅行，但决定留下来并讲完这些材料，因为班级规模庞大，意味着我们极度需要整整两周的时间来进行期末展示。

    关于那些期末小组项目：你们有两个选择。更好的选择是一个开放式的项目，在这个项目中你们分析一家真实公司的实际情报活动——例如，描绘SP集团如何主导国家能源情报，或者一家特定的初创公司如何在其领域内航行。如果你缺乏行业人脉或工作经验，你可以使用Canvas中提供的备用选项：关于“士卓曼（Straumann）”（一家瑞士中小企业）的案例研究。让我非常坦白地说：那些努力在一家真实公司上做开放式项目的小组，绝对会比那些仅仅展示预先包装好的士卓曼案例的小组得分更高。对于那些零经验的人来说，士卓曼仅仅是一个基本要求；如果你们想拿高分，就去做开放式的项目。

  - [20:07:27 - 20:12:42] **Finalizing Logbook Logistics and Forum Format**

    Addressing a question about the logbook format: There is no rigid template. You simply choose five topics from the semester. As discussed, a Level 1 entry just summarizes the academic theory (e.g., summarizing Carlson's article). A Level 2 entry connects that theory to your workplace (e.g., detailing a workshop your company ran). A Level 3 entry requires deep critical thinking, reflecting on the specific failures or problems encountered during that workplace activity and theorizing how it could have been fixed. You can focus your five entries entirely on the later, data-heavy analytical tools if you prefer. You can also email me your drafts mid-semester for feedback before final submission.

    Finally, regarding the forums: To accommodate the split between AI-users and experience-based learners, I will not use the clunky Canvas discussion board. Instead, I will create dedicated Google Docs. One document will be strictly for those using ChatGPT, and a separate document will be for those relying purely on personal experience. Please ensure you put your actual registered name and matriculation number on your entries so I can accurately grade you—no nicknames. Feel free to use creative formats like mind maps instead of writing essays. There is no fixed format; I am just looking for creativity and genuine knowledge sharing. I strictly warned the ChatGPT users not to pollute the experience-based document, or I will penalize them. After taking a quick class vote, we agreed to hold these forum challenges only every *alternate* week to avoid overwhelming you, and I will phase them out entirely by Week 8 or 9 so you can focus entirely on your group projects. That is all for today! For next week, please thoroughly read the Foresight Benchmarking Report, as your next "Challenge of the Day"—which carries high weightage—will be drawn directly from it. See you next week!

    解答关于日志格式的问题：没有僵化的模板。你只需从本学期中选择五个主题。正如所讨论的，第一级条目只是总结学术理论（例如，总结Carlson的文章）。第二级条目将该理论与你的工作场所联系起来（例如，详细描述你公司举办的一次研讨会）。第三级条目需要深度的批判性思维，反思在该工作场所活动中遇到的具体失败或问题，并从理论上探讨本可以如何解决。如果你愿意，你可以将你的五个条目完全集中在后期的、侧重数据分析的工具上。你也可以在学期中通过电子邮件将你的草稿发给我，以便在最终提交前获得反馈。

    最后，关于论坛：为了适应AI用户和基于经验的学习者之间的划分，我不会使用笨重的Canvas讨论板。相反，我将创建专门的Google Docs。一份文档将严格供那些使用ChatGPT的人使用，另一份独立的文档将供那些完全依赖个人经验的人使用。请确保在你的条目上写上你实际注册的姓名和学号，这样我才能准确地给你打分——不要用昵称。可以随意使用思维导图等创造性格式，而不是写长篇大论。没有固定的格式；我只是在寻找创造力和真正的知识分享。我严厉警告ChatGPT用户不要污染基于经验的文档，否则我会惩罚他们。在进行快速的课堂投票后，我们同意只在*每隔*一周举行这些论坛挑战，以避免给你们带来太大压力，我会在第8或第9周彻底取消它们，以便你们可以完全专注于小组项目。今天就到这里！下周，请仔细阅读《预见基准报告》（Foresight Benchmarking Report），因为你们的下一个“今日挑战”——权重很高——将直接从中提取。下周见！

  - [18:05:12 - 18:06:52] **Crisis Management vs. Foresighting**

    If you are thoroughly familiar with last week's content, let's try answering these questions I formulated just now. Let's tackle them individually. Is foresighting the exact same thing as crisis management? What do you all think? No? If the answer is no, why is it not crisis management? Yes, Kai, welcome back. How was your trip? Good? Okay, Kai says that crisis management is more about looking immediately at the situation or the company right after an event occurs. It is focused on acute problem-solving. Foresighting, on the other hand, looks at the process and the probability of what might actually pan out in the near future, perhaps over a ten-year horizon. So, as Kai accurately points out, foresighting looks at the long-term tail of events, whereas crisis management is very acute. Those are excellent points. Crisis management is indeed an acute problem-solving approach to immediately pressing problems. Foresighting is fundamentally long-term. You are still trying to solve a problem, but the problem is futuristic. Crisis management is inherently reactive; you are reacting to a fire that has already started. Foresighting is all about being proactive. Furthermore, foresighting isn't just about mitigating threats; it is equally about identifying and addressing future opportunities. A crisis response is almost entirely focused on mitigating short-term threats, not hunting for opportunities. Is that distinction clear? Great, Kai nailed that one.

    如果大家对上周的内容已经很熟悉了，让我们来尝试回答我刚刚准备的这些问题。我们一个个来。技术远见（Foresighting）和危机管理（Crisis Management）是完全一样的吗？大家怎么看？不是？如果不是，为什么它不是危机管理？好，Kai，欢迎回来，你的旅行怎么样？很好？好的。Kai 认为危机管理更多的是在事件发生后，立即关注局势或公司本身的状况。它侧重于解决突发的、紧迫的问题。另一方面，技术远见着眼于过程，以及在不久的将来（也许是十年内）可能实际发生的事情的概率。所以，正如 Kai 准确指出的那样，技术远见关注的是事件的长期发展，而危机管理是非常急迫的。这些观点非常好。危机管理确实是针对眼前紧迫问题的一种急性问题解决方法。技术远见从根本上来说是长期的。你仍然是在试图解决问题，但这个问题是未来才会发生的。危机管理本质上是被动的；你是在对已经燃起的大火做出反应。而技术远见则是关于主动出击。此外，技术远见不仅仅是关于减轻威胁；它同样关乎识别和抓住未来的机遇。危机应对几乎完全集中在减轻短期威胁上，而不是寻找机会。这个区别清楚了吗？很好，Kai 完美地回答了这个问题。

  - [18:06:52 - 18:08:27] **The Scope of Technology Intelligence**

    Moving on to the next concept. Is technology intelligence and foresighting a purely technological exercise? I ask this because if you were to Google "technology intelligence" right now, you might get a narrow definition. However, in the discussion forum, many of you rightly brought up concepts like competitor intelligence and social intelligence, creating many interesting threads focused on those broader aspects. So, is technology intelligence strictly limited to the technology itself? Exactly, it is not. If you listened attentively during our first class, I explained that it used to be just about technology back when the scope of strategic planning was narrow and the time horizon was short. But today, when the time horizon is long and the strategic scope is widened, you absolutely need to look at the market. What else must you look at apart from technology and the market? You must look at social factors and environmental factors. What else? Behavioral factors. Think back to the project we did for Prof Tan regarding the classroom environment; that was entirely about understanding behavioral shifts in learning. What else is there? There is one specific topic I want you all to point out because it connects closely to our previous discussions. Yes, ethics. Ethics plays an incredibly important role in technology intelligence. Many people erroneously exclude ethics from technology assessment, but unfortunately, that is a massive oversight. It must be part and parcel of the process. I am sure many of you studying AI have taken courses on AI ethics. Think about how foundational AI ethics is to the deployment of AI as a whole.

    继续下一个概念。技术情报（Technology Intelligence）和技术远见纯粹只是一项关于技术的活动吗？我问这个问题是因为，如果你现在去谷歌搜索“技术情报”，你可能会得到一个狭义的定义。然而，在讨论区中，你们很多人正确地提出了竞争对手情报和社会情报等概念，并围绕这些更广泛的方面展开了许多有趣的讨论。那么，技术情报真的仅仅局限于技术本身吗？完全正确，并非如此。如果你在第一节课上专心听讲了，我就解释过，在过去，当战略规划的范围很窄、时间跨度很短的时候，它确实只关注技术。但在今天，当时间跨度变长、战略范围扩大时，你绝对需要关注市场。除了技术和市场，你还需要关注什么？你必须关注社会因素和环境因素。还有什么？行为因素。回想一下我们为 Tan 教授做的关于课堂环境的项目；那完全是为了理解学习行为的转变。还有什么？有一个特定的话题我希望大家指出来，因为它与我们之前的讨论密切相关。是的，伦理（Ethics）。伦理在技术情报中扮演着极其重要的角色。许多人错误地将伦理排除在技术评估之外，遗憾的是，这是一个巨大的疏忽。它必须是整个过程中不可或缺的一部分。我相信你们中很多学习 AI 的同学都上过 AI 伦理课。想想看，AI 伦理对于 AI 整体的部署有多么基础和关键。

  - [18:08:27 - 18:13:21] **Visionary Leaders and the Delphi Method**

    Next question: Is foresighting simply about a single visionary leader sitting at the top, handing down directions and speculations? There was a great forum post on this specific dynamic by Rini. Where is Rini? Okay, great. Rini posted about whether foresighting is just a top-down directive from a visionary leader. Let's discuss that. One student pointed out that while a strategic vision often comes from top management, the actual foresighting process is better initiated by R&D management or business unit leaders on the ground, though they obviously need higher management support to execute it. That is a very accurate answer. It should involve insights from R&D and other operational managers. Another student added, building on our last class, that foresighting can and should be a bottom-up approach where those doing the actual working and researching realize what the emerging trends are. That is also true. As I emphasized before, foresighting is a comprehensive process, and that process requires involving all kinds of stakeholders, exactly as Carlson's article detailed. If an organization relies solely on one visionary leader giving all the direction, there is no harm—provided that leader is an absolute, infallible genius. But in reality, that seldom happens. Rini's post critically examined what happens when an organization is entirely driven by one leader. What happens when that leader leaves? Or worse, what if that one leader is deeply flawed, highly commanding, and steering the company in completely the wrong direction while the rest of the industry is moving differently? It is true that many companies, especially Small and Medium Enterprises (SMEs), operate this way because they simply lack the bandwidth or resources to engage in formal, broad-based foresighting activities. The leader decides, and the company follows. But does that mean formal foresighting ignores visionaries? No. In formal foresighting, there is a prominent technique called the Delphi method, which we will learn about in detail after the midterm break. The Delphi method is all about systematically seeking the opinions of industry leaders and experts. But crucially, it is not just one leader. You consult many leaders across the industry. You collect both quantitative and qualitative evidence to iteratively decide how the industry is likely to evolve. You absolutely need to talk to visionaries and leaders, but you do not let one single person direct the entire narrative. You use structured processes to seek consensus even among the experts. So, to conclude on ethics from earlier, someone correctly noted that applying ethics allows for transparency and helps break down barriers, ensuring that everyone is agreeable on the fundamental principles of what should or should not be developed. The question is, where does ethics come into the picture? Initial stages, middle stages, or later stages? Some might think the initial stage is too early to apply ethical constraints, but in reality, you need an ethical direction set from the very beginning, even if detailed ethical assessments happen a bit later as the technology's path becomes clearer. Okay, Seng Meng is here, and I don't want to eat into his time any further. I will address some of the remaining forum pointers later. Let's welcome Seng Meng. He is an incredibly busy person, constantly traveling and working, but he still made his way here today to share his insights. Thank you so much, Seng Meng. Please, let's get you set up. You want to use your laptop, right? Here is the HDMI cable.

    下一个问题：技术远见仅仅是指一位高高在上的有远见的领导者，向下传达指示和预测吗？关于这种特定的动态，Rini 在论坛上发了一篇很好的帖子。Rini 在哪里？好的，很好。Rini 帖子的主题是：技术远见是否仅仅是来自有远见的领导者的自上而下的指令。我们来讨论一下。一位同学指出，虽然战略愿景通常来自最高管理层，但实际的技术远见流程最好由一线的研发管理层或业务部门领导来发起，当然，他们显然需要高层管理的支持来执行。这是一个非常准确的答案。它应该包含来自研发和其他运营管理者的洞察。另一位同学补充说，基于我们上一节课的内容，技术远见可以也应该是一种自下而上的方法，让那些进行实际工作和研究的人意识到新兴趋势是什么。这也是对的。正如我之前强调的，技术远见是一个综合性的过程，这个过程需要所有相关利益者的参与，这正是 Carlson 文章中详细说明的。如果一个组织仅仅依赖一位有远见的领导者来指明所有方向，这并没有什么坏处——前提是这位领导者是一个绝对不会犯错的超级天才。但在现实中，这种情况很少发生。Rini 的帖子批判性地探讨了当一个组织完全由一位领导者驱动时会发生什么。当那位领导者离开时会怎样？或者更糟的是，如果这位领导者有着严重的缺陷，非常专横，并且在整个行业都在朝不同方向发展时，把公司引向了完全错误的方向，那该怎么办？确实，许多公司，特别是中小企业（SMEs），是按照这种方式运作的，因为他们根本没有精力或资源来参与正式的、广泛的技术远见活动。领导者做决定，公司就照做。但这是否意味着正式的技术远见会忽略有远见的人呢？不。在正式的技术远见中，有一种重要的方法叫做德尔菲法（Delphi method），我们将在期中考试后详细学习。德尔菲法的核心是系统地寻求行业领导者和专家的意见。但关键是，它不仅仅是一位领导者。你需要咨询行业内的多位领导者。你收集定量和定性的证据，通过迭代来决定行业可能如何演变。你绝对需要与有远见的人和领导者交流，但你不能让某一个人主导整个方向。你需要使用结构化的流程，在专家之间寻求共识。那么，回到早些时候关于伦理的结论，有人正确地指出，应用伦理可以提高透明度，有助于打破壁垒，确保每个人都在“应该开发什么”或“不应该开发什么”的基本原则上达成一致。问题是，伦理应该在哪个阶段介入？初始阶段、中间阶段还是后期阶段？有些人可能认为在初始阶段施加伦理约束为时过早，但实际上，你需要从一开始就设定一个伦理方向，即使详细的伦理评估是在技术路径变得更清晰之后的稍晚阶段进行的。好的，Seng Meng 到了，我不想再占用他的时间了。我稍后会处理论坛上剩下的一些问题。让我们欢迎 Seng Meng。他是一个非常忙碌的人，经常出差和工作，但他今天还是特意赶来分享他的见解。非常感谢你，Seng Meng。请进，我们来帮你设置一下。你想用你的笔记本电脑，对吧？这是 HDMI 线。
