    但现在回到我们要开始的地方。至少现在你能回答这个问题了吗？所以如果你要发起 [TI]，你会做的第一步是什么？去寻找信息。对你的公司是什么有个概念？我该怎么做？首先是那个。然后是“什么结构会行得通？什么结构行不通？”我如何为此寻找来源，然后把大家聚在一起，得出那个问题？你要研究的问题是什么？然后是寻找信息，以及你是否整合了等等，等等，等等。你们提到的所有都是[其中的一部分]，但在任何事情之前必须发生更高层次的事情……除了领域[专家]，她在第一轮赢了。她总是从上面看，对吧？当她能描绘出那个时，清楚了吗？所以这就是你在公司开始 TI 活动的方式，理解组织。
    如果有任何问题，我会在这里。休息期间有一个问题。好的，开始写你们的 Logbook，如果你有任何想看反馈的问题，继续发给我。这就是它的运作方式，因为截止日期在最后，请提交 **一个文件**，其中包含所有的周。不要提交 5 个不同的文件。用你的学号命名你的文件。我的工作方式，上学期上过我课的人知道：如果你在写 Logbook，发给我。我会给你反馈以改进。你可以开始在上面构建，不要把所有的逻辑[草稿]都发给我……这就像把你的分数送人，对吧？别那样做。给反馈，在上面工作，然后就可以了。就是这样。如果你完成了 Logbook 并且在课堂上参与，60% 的评分就完成了。那是最终项目，对吧？所以尽量完成所有事情。
    下周我会给，我会给一篇无聊的论文让你们读。我告诉过你们，对吧？我不会忘记的。你们读那篇无聊的论文。这将是一篇。好的，我会为那些上过 **MT5007** 的人提一下。记得我提过标准作业（Standard Work）是必修的 Logbook 文章之一吗？你能相信尽管我在课堂上讲了一百万次，我仍然收到至少 5 份没有标准作业的提交吗？好的，不要重复这个。我不认为所有学生都在这里，但如果你在听我说，我希望如此。所以我希望你们都读那篇特别无聊的论文，你们有两周的时间读，但在下周之后实际上是三周，接下来的几周我看不到你们。所以读它，我很确定你无法一次读完。那篇论文……你会看到浏览器睡着了。所以再读一遍。
    我想要从论文中得到的是：**尝试以思维导图（Mind Map）或框图或图片的形式综合论文的关键信息。** 这就是分析师所做的。读无聊透顶的东西，从中提取有价值的信息，并以图形形式呈现。这将是每个人都要做的一个必修 Logbook [条目]。对于那些不在这里的人，有一个……对于那些在睡觉的人，后排醒醒，还有没在听我说话的人：每个人在 Logbook 提交中都应该有一个必修的 Logbook，那就是读我给的那篇无聊的论文。我不会叫它无聊的论文。它是一篇非常有价值的论文。那是作者的名字……**Lichtenthaler**。论文并综合有价值的……不，你需要知道什么是有价值的，什么是没价值的。这也必须重要，好的。什么是最有价值的信息？把它拉出来，以非常简洁、结构化的思维导图或图形形式呈现。对此有任何疑问吗？因为下周我不能当面讲这个。我在告诉你们，给出所有的……有任何疑问吗？现在问。
    *学生：* 是什么论文？
    *教授：* 如果你想……如果你认为你已经给出了足够的……我知道那篇论文，所以我知道她已经涵盖了足够的信息，但如果你认为某些章节你觉得重要，或者如果你遗漏了某些东西因为你觉得它不重要，你可以写。但不应该……没必要。你的 Logbook 没有固定的格式。我不会限制你说只能写这么多页。随意，因为那是为了测试你有多创新。创新不应该被限制在某一点之外。这就是为什么我不限制。是的，试图购买技术。
    *学生：* 是的，我想是这样，但我需要去……因为他写了 2 篇我用的论文。一篇是关于被动学习的，那是他的游戏。我会让你……
    *教授：* 我们刚刚做了那个。我需要找出来，因为有几位欧洲作者。它是 **Lichtenthaler** 写的，我就知道这么多。我会告诉你们，因为我不……所以那是唯一必修的。那是唯一必修的，好的。它就在那个东西上，只是有两篇论文。我不想搞混了。我去下一节课后会告诉你们。还有别的吗，说出来。
## Week 5
  - [18:00:19 - 18:03:16] **Session Setup, Chinese New Year Chat, and Agenda Overview**

    Professor Annapoornima begins the session by ensuring the technical setup is functioning, specifically enabling screen sharing for visibility and starting the recording. While waiting for the class to settle in, she engages in a bit of casual conversation, asking how many students are traveling for the upcoming Chinese New Year break, requesting a show of hands or thumbs up.

    She then outlines the agenda for the evening. The plan is to start with a summary of the previous week's content because, although they covered most of the Week 4 slides, a few sections remain outstanding. These remaining slides will naturally bridge into the new topic of Knowledge Management. The structure for the class involves finishing the Week 4 review first, followed by a guest lecture from Professor René Rohrbeck scheduled from 6:15 PM to 7:15 PM. After the guest lecture, the class will take a break before resuming with the remaining lecture slides, covering as much ground as possible regarding Knowledge Management.

    Annapoornima 教授首先检查了技术设置，确保屏幕共享已启用并开始录制。在等待学生就座时，她与大家闲聊了几句，询问有多少人计划在即将到来的农历新年假期出行，并请大家举手或点赞示意。

    随后，她概述了当晚的议程。计划是先总结上周的内容，因为尽管他们已经讲完了第四周的大部分幻灯片，但仍有一些部分未涉及。这些剩余的幻灯片将自然过渡到“知识管理”这一新主题。课程安排是先完成第四周的复习，随后在下午 6:15 到 7:15 进行 René Rohrbeck 教授的客座讲座。客座讲座结束后，班级将休息片刻，然后继续讲授剩余的幻灯片，尽可能多地涵盖关于知识管理的内容。

  - [18:03:16 - 18:05:21] **Recap of Week 4: The Systemic and Systematic Framework**

    Professor Annapoornima initiates a review by asking the class what they recall from the previous week's lecture. Student Tan Kai Beng volunteers, explaining that they covered the overarching structure of Technology Intelligence (TI) from a managerial perspective. He notes that they discussed how to conduct foresight and TI activities, including the management hierarchy, the mission or goal structure, and the tools involved, although they had stopped short of diving deeply into the specific tools.

    The Professor validates this and asks the class to explain why the framework is described as both "systemic" and "systematic." When prompted, Tan Kai Beng elaborates that "systemic" refers to the holistic structure—the entire ecosystem of the process—while "systematic" refers to the step-by-step execution of individual activities, such as data analysis, dissemination, and collection. The Professor agrees, emphasizing that TI is not just about the direct intelligence activities but relies heavily on the indirect activities—management, mission, and structure—that enable the system to function.

    Annapoornima 教授通过提问开启了复习环节，询问学生们还记得上周讲了什么。学生 Tan Kai Beng 主动回答说，他们从管理者的角度涵盖了技术情报（TI）的总体结构。他指出，他们讨论了如何开展前瞻和 TI 活动，包括管理层级、使命或目标结构以及涉及的工具，尽管他们还没深入探讨具体的工具。

    教授确认了这一点，并请班级解释为什么该框架被描述为既是“系统性（Systemic）”又是“体系化（Systematic）”的。在提示下，Tan Kai Beng 阐述道，“系统性”指的是整体结构——即流程的整个生态系统——而“体系化”指的是逐步执行的具体活动，如数据分析、传播和收集。教授对此表示赞同，并强调技术情报不仅仅是直接的情报活动，还严重依赖于那些使其能够运作的间接活动——即管理、使命和结构。

  - [18:05:21 - 18:07:31] **Deep Dive: Direct vs. Indirect Activities in Technology Intelligence**

    Sharing her slides, Professor Annapoornima directs the students' attention to the conceptual framework diagram (referencing Slide 5/6 of Week 4). She points out that while many people focus exclusively on the "Direct Activities" on the right side of the diagram (Processing, Analysis, Dissemination), the "Indirect Activities" on the left—Management, Mission/Goals, and Structure—are equally critical. These indirect elements enable the direct activities to happen.

    She elaborates on the terminology: the framework is "systemic" because it encompasses every element required to orchestrate the system, including resource allocation, hiring, and directing the mission. It is "systematic" because it follows a logical, sequential process where one step feeds into the next. She reminds the class that they had previously covered the Mission and Management aspects and asks them to recall specific tools or templates associated with defining the Mission.

    Annapoornima 教授分享了她的幻灯片，引导学生关注概念框架图（参考第四周幻灯片第 5/6 页）。她指出，虽然许多人只关注图表右侧的“直接活动”（处理、分析、传播），但左侧的“间接活动”——管理、使命/目标和结构——同样至关重要。这些间接要素是直接活动得以开展的基础。

    她详细解释了相关术语：该框架之所以是“系统性”的，是因为它包含了协调系统所需的每一个要素，包括资源分配、招聘和指导使命。它是“体系化”的，因为它遵循逻辑顺序，一步紧扣一步。她提醒全班，他们之前已经涵盖了使命和管理方面的内容，并请他们回忆与定义使命相关的具体工具或模板。

  - [18:07:31 - 18:09:46] **The Information Needs Template (Kerr et al.)**

    Student Tan Yi Chun identifies the "Information Needs Template" as the key tool introduced in the last lecture. The Professor asks for clarification on its utility. Tan Yi Chun explains that this template maps to the left side of the framework, helping to identify potential application areas, define sources, and plan how to engage with them.

    Professor Annapoornima confirms this, referencing the template by Kerr et al. (Slide 14/15). She highlights its importance in framing the problem statement. The template is used during brainstorming sessions to identify gaps and needs—specifically determining what the organization needs to know and why. This is not just about defining the problem but also structuring the search process by leveraging the network of people involved in the workshop. It bridges the gap between management's strategic requirements and the practical search for intelligence.

    学生 Tan Yi Chun 指出“信息需求模板”是上节课介绍的关键工具。教授询问了它的用途。Tan Yi Chun 解释说，该模板对应框架的左侧，有助于识别潜在的应用领域，定义来源，并规划如何与这些来源接触。

    Annapoornima 教授确认了这一点，并引用了 Kerr 等人的模板（幻灯片 14/15）。她强调了其在构建问题陈述中的重要性。该模板用于头脑风暴会议，以识别差距和需求——具体确定组织需要知道什么以及为什么需要知道。这不仅是关于定义问题，还在于通过利用参与研讨会的人际网络来构建搜索过程。它在管理层的战略需求与实际的情报搜索之间架起了桥梁。

  - [18:09:46 - 18:12:19] **Intelligence Hierarchies and Organizational Structures**

    The Professor continues the summary by reviewing the hierarchy of intelligence needs (Slide 11), asking "Who, What, Where, When, Why, and How?" across various dimensions—social, economic, political, and legal—not just technological. She reiterates that intelligence work serves to identify opportunities and threats through primary and secondary sources.

    She then moves to the topic of organizational structure, recalling their discussion on the "Single-Node" versus "Multi-Node" approaches (Slide 23). She notes that the choice of structure often depends on the industry context and business model. For instance, knowledge-intensive industries increasingly favor multi-node approaches to handle complexity. She acknowledges the students' forum discussions on this topic, noting that many shared valuable insights from their own organizations regarding these structural dynamics.

    教授继续总结，回顾了情报需求的层级（幻灯片 11），即在社会、经济、政治和法律等各个维度——而不仅仅是技术维度——提出“谁、什么、哪里、何时、为什么和如何”的问题。她重申，情报工作旨在通过一手和二手来源识别机会和威胁。

    随后，她转向组织结构的话题，回顾了他们关于“单节点”与“多节点”方法的讨论（幻灯片 23）。她指出，结构的选择往往取决于行业背景和商业模式。例如，知识密集型行业越来越倾向于采用多节点方法来应对复杂性。她对学生在论坛上关于这一话题的讨论表示认可，并指出许多人分享了来自各自组织的关于这些结构动态的有价值见解。

  - [18:12:19 - 18:14:47] **Introduction of Guest Lecturer: Professor René Rohrbeck**

    As the guest lecturer, Professor René Rohrbeck, joins the call, Annapoornima welcomes him warmly. She explains to him that she was summarizing the previous week's content while waiting. She notes that although it is only Week 5, they scheduled his lecture early due to the upcoming Chinese New Year break.

    After René shares his slides, Annapoornima formally introduces him to the class. She highlights that René is a Professor of Strategy at EDHEC Business School and the Director of the Chair for Foresight, Innovation, and Transformation. She mentions that the class has already engaged with his work, specifically a benchmarking report and a recent paper on AI in Foresight. She also enthusiastically recommends his website and podcasts, admitting she has become his "marketing guy" because the resources are so valuable. She then hands the floor over to him to discuss "AI for Foresight."

    随着客座讲师 René Rohrbeck 教授加入通话，Annapoornima 热情地欢迎了他。她向他解释说，自己在等待期间正在总结上周的内容。她指出，尽管现在只是第五周，但由于即将到来的农历新年假期，他们特意将他的讲座安排得较早。

    在 René 分享幻灯片后，Annapoornima 正式向全班介绍了他。她强调 René 是法国北方高等商学院（EDHEC）的战略学教授，也是前瞻、创新与转型教席的主任。她提到班级已经学习过他的作品，特别是基准测试报告和最近一篇关于人工智能在前瞻中应用的论文。她还热情推荐了他的网站和播客，笑称自己已经成了他的“营销员”，因为这些资源非常有价值。随后，她将讲台交给他，以此展开关于“人工智能用于前瞻”的讨论。

  - [18:14:47 - 18:16:31] **René Rohrbeck: Background and the Intersection of Strategy and Foresight**

    René begins by setting a conversational tone, preferring a chat over a formal lecture. He provides background on his career, noting he spent around eight years in the industry working in strategy. His focus has always been looking from the "tail towards the front," figuring out how to integrate Foresight into Strategy.

    He describes himself as a pragmatist who constantly asks what Foresight actually brings to decision-making, innovation, and new insights. Currently, he runs the EDHEC Center for Net Positive Business, helping organizations transition toward a regenerative future using foresight methodologies. He indicates that this practical lens will shape his discussion on how AI is applied in foresight today.

    René 首先定下了对话的基调，表示更喜欢聊天而不是正式讲座。他介绍了自己的职业背景，提到他在行业内从事战略工作约八年。他的关注点始终是从“尾部看向前部”，思考如何将前瞻整合到战略中。

    他将自己描述为一个实用主义者，不断追问前瞻究竟能为决策、创新和新见解带来什么。目前，他负责 EDHEC 净正向商业中心（Center for Net Positive Business），利用前瞻方法帮助组织向再生未来转型。他指出，这一实践视角将贯穿他关于当前人工智能如何应用于前瞻的讨论。

  - [18:16:31 - 18:20:07] **Slido Poll 1: Assessing the Class's AI Usage**

    René launches a Slido poll to gauge the students' current level of AI usage. The options range from avoiding AI to systematically experimenting with it for all tasks. As the results come in, he notes a split, with about 40-50% of the class falling into the "systematically experimenting" category.

    He remarks that this is a relatively high adoption rate compared to corporate settings, where usage is often lower, especially when filtered for "productive use." He touches upon the concept of the "Jagged Edge of AI"—the phenomenon where AI can be revolutionary one day and produce "utter gibberish" the next. He emphasizes that navigating this inconsistency is a major challenge for professionals, as they must determine when AI is a reliable research assistant or sparring partner and when it is hallucinating or taking shortcuts.

    René 发起了一个 Slido 投票，以评估学生目前的人工智能使用水平。选项范围从避免使用人工智能到在所有任务中系统地尝试使用。随着结果的揭晓，他注意到出现了分歧，班上约 40-50% 的人属于“系统性尝试”这一类。

    他评论说，与企业环境相比，这是一个相对较高的采用率，因为在企业中，特别是当过滤掉非“生产性使用”时，使用率往往较低。他提到了“人工智能的锯齿状边缘（Jagged Edge of AI）”这一概念——即人工智能可能某天具有革命性，而第二天却产出“完全的胡言乱语”的现象。他强调，驾驭这种不稳定性是专业人士面临的一大挑战，因为他们必须判断人工智能何时是可靠的研究助手或陪练伙伴，何时又是在产生幻觉或走捷径。

  - [18:20:07 - 18:22:04] **OECD Study Data: The Confidence Gap in AI Skills**

    René presents data from a recent joint study by the OECD and the World Economic Forum (WEF) regarding AI in foresight. He focuses on a specific data point asking respondents if they possess the relevant skills to use AI in foresight work. He points out a surprising finding: the private sector respondents reported close to 100% agreement that they have the necessary skills.

    René expresses skepticism about this high number, contrasting it with his field experience talking to corporate strategy departments where confidence is generally lower. He suggests the data might be biased because surveys often attract respondents who are already interested in the topic. He raises a critical question about "reflective users"—how many of these confident users are actually critically assessing the limitations of the tools they are using?

    René 展示了经合组织（OECD）和世界经济论坛（WEF）最近关于前瞻中的人工智能的联合研究数据。他重点关注一个具体的数据点，该点询问受访者是否具备在前瞻工作中使用人工智能的相关技能。他指出了一个令人惊讶的发现：私营部门的受访者报告了接近 100% 的同意率，认为自己具备必要的技能。

    René 对这一高得惊人的数字表示怀疑，将其与他在实地与企业战略部门交流的经验进行了对比，因为在现实中人们的信心通常较低。他认为数据可能存在偏差，因为调查往往吸引那些已经对该主题感兴趣的受访者。他提出了一个关于“反思性用户”的关键问题——在这些自信的用户中，有多少人真正批判性地评估了他们所使用工具的局限性？

  - [18:22:04 - 18:24:12] **Slido Poll 2: The Dominance of OpenAI**

    René conducts a second poll asking which specific AI tools the students are using. The results show OpenAI (ChatGPT) as the clear frontrunner, with some presence of German models catching up. René notes this mirrors the global market share distribution, where major players constantly leapfrog each other in capabilities. He transitions to the more nuanced question: not just *which* tool is used, but *for what specific task* is each tool deployed?

    René 进行了第二次投票，询问学生具体使用哪些人工智能工具。结果显示 OpenAI（ChatGPT）明显处于领先地位，还有一些德国模型正在迎头赶上。René 指出，这反映了全球市场份额的分布，主要参与者在能力上不断相互超越。他随后转向一个更微妙的问题：不仅是使用*哪种*工具，而是每种工具被部署用于*什么具体任务*？

  - [18:24:12 - 18:27:15] **Mapping AI Tools to Foresight Phases: A Community of Practice Project**

    René introduces a framework developed with an industry community of practice. They map AI tools against the foresight process to benchmark time savings and efficiency. The process is divided into three phases:

    1. **Perceiving (Scanning):** Using AI to scan and understand trends and factors shaping the future.

    2. **Prospecting (Scenarios):** Using AI to build scenario narratives. René contrasts this with the past, where scenario projects took 3 months and significant budgets to produce narratives or videos. Now, AI can generate these assets rapidly.

    3. **Probing (Strategy/Action):** Moving quickly to seize opportunities, such as identifying acquisition targets or innovation partners.

       He emphasizes that the goal is to shorten the cycle from scanning to investment, asking how much we can compress the timeline from "years" to "weeks" using better data and AI.

    René 介绍了一个与行业实践社区共同开发的框架。他们将人工智能工具映射到前瞻流程中，以基准测试节省的时间和效率。该流程分为三个阶段：

    1. **感知（扫描）：** 利用人工智能扫描和理解塑造未来的趋势和因素。

    2. **勘探（情景）：** 利用人工智能构建情景叙事。René 将其与过去进行了对比，过去的情景项目需要 3 个月和大量预算才能制作出叙事或视频。现在，人工智能可以快速生成这些资产。

    3. **探索（战略/行动）：** 迅速采取行动抓住机会，例如确定收购目标或创新合作伙伴。

       他强调，目标是缩短从扫描到投资的周期，并提出一个问题：利用更好的数据和人工智能，我们能在多大程度上将时间线从“几年”压缩到“几周”。

  - [18:27:15 - 18:31:34] **Low Adoption of Predictive Modeling and Forecasting**

    René returns to the OECD data to discuss the adoption rates of AI in specific activities like Horizon Scanning, Trend Analysis, and Predictive Modeling. Professor Annapoornima interrupts with a question, expressing surprise that the adoption of AI for "Predictive Modeling or Forecasting" is reported as very low, given AI's natural strength in data tasks.

    René agrees it is surprising and offers two explanations. First, it may be a flaw in the questionnaire design—organizations not doing predictive modeling at all (with or without AI) might simply not check the box. Second, sophisticated predictive modeling is often a niche activity limited to specific industries, like big oil companies that have large teams dedicated to modeling energy markets. These niche players definitely use AI agents for real-time monitoring, but they represent a small fraction of the overall sample.

    René 回到经合组织的数据，讨论人工智能在地平线扫描、趋势分析和预测建模等具体活动中的采用率。Annapoornima 教授插话提问，表示对于“预测建模或预测”中人工智能的采用率被报告得很低感到惊讶，因为人工智能在数据任务方面具有天然优势。

    René 同意这令人惊讶，并提供了两个解释。首先，这可能是问卷设计的缺陷——根本不做预测建模（无论是否使用人工智能）的组织可能只是没有勾选该选项。其次，复杂的预测建模通常是仅限于特定行业的利基活动，例如大型石油公司拥有专门的团队来模拟能源市场。这些利基参与者肯定使用人工智能代理进行实时监控，但他们在整个样本中只占很小的一部分。

  - [18:31:34 - 18:32:18] **Final Poll Setup: Ranking AI Benefits**

    René sets up a final ranking task for the students. He asks them to rank the parts of the foresight process where they believe AI can provide the most benefit—whether in time-saving, efficiency gains, or quality improvements. He guides them on how to click and drag the options to submit their rankings as the first responses begin to trickle in.

    René 为学生安排了最后的排名任务。他请大家对前瞻流程的各个部分进行排名，指出他们认为人工智能在哪些方面能提供最大的益处——无论是在节省时间、提高效率还是改善质量方面。随着第一批回复开始陆续进来，他指导大家如何通过点击和拖动选项来提交排名。

  - [18:33:04 - 18:37:35] **The Three Benefits of AI in Foresight: Speed, Efficiency, and Quality**

    Professor René Rohrbeck reflects on the ranking task he just assigned, acknowledging that asking students to rank the benefits of AI is inherently difficult. He breaks down the value proposition into three categories. First is speed: while AI delivers results quickly, he questions if speed alone creates organizational value, especially if the output requires extensive verification, which negates the time saved. The second benefit is resource optimization. He uses the example of a large oil company with 50 analysts; if AI can achieve the same results with 40, the company saves resources, though this may not be the primary driver for all organizations.

    The third and most interesting factor is quality. In human-based processes, analysts are limited by time and cognitive capacity—typically processing only the top 5 or 6 reports manually. AI can crunch vastly more data, clustering trends and visualizing data much faster. However, René warns of the "garbage in, garbage out" problem: if the AI is fed poor-quality reports, the analysis will be flawed. He also points out a strategic dilemma: if AI democratizes high-quality analysis, basic consulting tasks become commodities. If everyone uses AI, having "good" vs. "not-so-good" junior analysts makes little difference. However, for high-stakes tasks like predictive modeling or scenario development—such as investing in a new oil field or factory—human oversight remains crucial. Decision-makers cannot rely on a "black box"; they need transparency and a deep grasp of the models.

    René Rohrbeck 教授对刚刚布置的排名任务进行了反思，承认要求学生对 AI 的益处进行排名本质上是困难的。他将价值主张分解为三类。首先是速度：虽然 AI 能迅速提供结果，但他质疑仅凭速度是否能创造组织价值，特别是如果输出结果需要大量验证，这会抵消节省下来的时间。第二个益处是资源优化。他以一家拥有 50 名分析师的大型石油公司为例；如果 AI 能用 40 人达到同样的结果，公司就能节省资源，尽管这可能并非所有组织的首要驱动力。

    第三个也是最有趣的因素是质量。在基于人工的流程中，分析师受限于时间和认知能力——通常只能手动处理最重要的 5 到 6 份报告。AI 可以处理海量数据，更快速地聚类趋势和可视化数据。然而，René 警告了“垃圾进，垃圾出”的问题：如果给 AI 投喂的是低质量报告，分析结果也会有缺陷。他还指出了一个战略困境：如果 AI 让高质量分析变得普及，基础咨询任务将变成大路货。如果每个人都使用 AI，拥有“优秀”还是“一般”的初级分析师差别就不大了。然而，对于预测建模或情景开发等高风险任务——例如投资新油田或工厂——人工监督仍然至关重要。决策者不能依赖“黑箱”，他们需要透明度以及对模型的深刻理解。

  - [18:37:35 - 18:41:58] **Case Study: Siemens and the Future of Work**

    René introduces a case study involving Siemens (referred to as "Zmans" in the raw audio, corrected here to the likely subject context). The company needed to understand technology and business trends for the next 10 to 20 years to define future job profiles and apprenticeship curriculums. This is a complex strategy task involving scanning, analysis, and curriculum design. René notes that while the "Scanning" phase works well with AI, the "Analysis" phase saw dramatic efficiency gains. Previously, building a full trend profile took an analyst 3 to 4 hours; with AI, this was cut down to about one hour, allowing for the rapid creation of a "Trend Radar."

    The most significant impact was in the "Act" phase, specifically in building education curricula. Traditionally, designing a new course would require a professor to work for three months. In this case, AI could draft the course outline, session structures, and examination methods almost instantly. René summarizes that while the front-end scoping of the project still requires heavy human agency to define *where* to look, the later stages of execution are increasingly becoming a 50-50 split between human and AI, or even AI-dominant.

    René 介绍了一个涉及西门子（Siemens）的案例研究。该公司需要了解未来 10 到 20 年的技术和商业趋势，以定义未来的职位概况和学徒课程。这是一项复杂的战略任务，涉及扫描、分析和课程设计。René 指出，虽然“扫描”阶段利用 AI 效果良好，但“分析”阶段的效率提升尤为显著。以前，构建完整的趋势档案需要分析师花费 3 到 4 小时；利用 AI，这一时间缩短至约一小时，从而能够快速创建“趋势雷达”。

    最大的影响发生在“行动”阶段，特别是在构建教育课程方面。传统上，设计一门新课程需要教授工作三个月。而在本案例中，AI 几乎可以瞬间起草课程大纲、课程结构和考核方式。René 总结道，虽然项目的前端范围界定仍需要大量人工介入来确定*看哪里*，但在后续的执行阶段，人工与 AI 的比例正日益变为 50-50，甚至由 AI 主导。

  - [18:41:58 - 18:45:07] **Principles of Human-AI Collaboration: Agency and Accountability**

    René discusses the necessary principles for guiding Human-AI collaboration. He observes that many users do not take a step back to ask the fundamental question: "How much mandate do I give the AI?" He contrasts using AI as a preliminary research assistant versus relying on it for the final answer. He argues that users must define these principles *before* engaging with the tools.

    He outlines specific principles derived from their research. In the "Scan" phase, AI provides breadth, but humans must verify the results—one cannot simply copy-paste trend lists. He highlights the risk of hallucination and the use of low-quality, non-peer-reviewed sources by Large Language Models (LLMs). Bias control and traceability are strictly human responsibilities. He shares the common experience of finding a "super interesting" insight generated by AI, only to dig for the source and realize it was a hallucination. Therefore, traceability and fact-checking remain essential human tasks in this workflow.

    René 讨论了指导人机协作的必要原则。他观察到，许多用户没有退一步去问那个根本性的问题：“我给予 AI 多大的授权？”他对比了将 AI 用作初步研究助手与依赖其提供最终答案这两种情况。他认为，用户必须在通过工具进行工作*之前*就定义好这些原则。

    他概述了基于他们研究的具体原则。在“扫描”阶段，AI 提供了广度，但人类必须验证结果——不能简单地复制粘贴趋势列表。他强调了大型语言模型（LLM）产生幻觉以及使用低质量、未经同行评审来源的风险。偏差控制和可追溯性严格来说是人类的责任。他分享了一种常见的经历：发现 AI 生成了一个“超级有趣”的见解，结果深入挖掘来源时却发现那是幻觉。因此，可追溯性和事实核查在该工作流程中仍然是必不可少的人工任务。

  - [18:45:07 - 18:50:34] **The "Nightmare Competitor" Strategy Retreat**

    René shares a recent engagement with a global Tier 1 IT transformation company (a major SAP partner). The company, having enjoyed 40 years of stability and high margins in the ERP implementation market, held a strategy retreat for 80 partners and 80 young leaders. To challenge their complacency, René's team used "Scenario-based Strategizing." They started by using Slido to poll the participants on their beliefs about AI's impact by 2035, then contrasted those beliefs with a forecast to "unhinge" them and create uncertainty.

    Once the participants realized the future was uncertain, they were open to scenario planning. René explains that in the past, budget and time constraints would have limited them to generic scenarios. However, using AI, they built highly customized, industry-specific scenarios in less than half a day. They also utilized a "Nightmare Competitor" exercise, asking partners to imagine a competitor that could destroy their business model, which helps generate guiding principles for their own strategy.

    René 分享了最近与一家全球一级 IT 转型公司（主要的 SAP 合作伙伴）的合作经历。该公司在企业资源规划（ERP）实施市场享受了 40 年的稳定和高利润，近期为 80 名合伙人和 80 名年轻领导者举办了战略务虚会。为了打破他们的自满情绪，René 的团队使用了“基于情景的战略制定”方法。他们首先使用 Slido 调查参与者对 2035 年 AI 影响的看法，然后将这些看法与预测进行对比，以“动摇”他们并制造不确定性。

    一旦参与者意识到未来是不确定的，他们就愿意接受情景规划了。René 解释说，在过去，预算和时间限制只能让他们做一些通用的情景。然而，利用 AI，他们在不到半天的时间里构建了高度定制化、针对特定行业的情景。他们还利用了“噩梦竞争对手”练习，要求合伙人设想一个可能摧毁他们商业模式的竞争对手，这有助于为他们自己的战略生成指导原则。

  - [18:50:34 - 18:52:41] **Scenario Video: "The Algorithmic Shakeout" (2035)**

    René plays a video scenario generated for the client, titled "The Algorithmic Shakeout." The video describes the year 2035, where platform giants like SAP, Microsoft, and Salesforce have released "autonomous migration agents." These agents automatically map architecture, rewrite legacy code, test, and deploy systems overnight while clients sleep.

    The narrative depicts a world where Requests for Proposals (RFPs) and billable hours are obsolete. Switching providers is as easy as a click, and transparency is absolute. The market splits into two: a handful of AI-native giants operating with near-zero marginal costs and 30-45% operating margins, and old incumbents struggling with high costs. The talent landscape shifts drastically—junior roles disappear, and demand concentrates on "Trust Brokers," "System Architects," and "AI Governors." The video concludes with an existential question for the firm (referred to as "Delaware" or similar in the context): "What do you do that an algorithm never can?"

    René 播放了一段为客户生成的名为“算法大洗牌”的视频情景。视频描述了 2035 年，SAP、微软和 Salesforce 等平台巨头发布了“自主迁移代理”。这些代理在客户睡觉时，通宵自动绘制架构图、重写遗留代码、测试并部署系统。

    旁白描绘了一个提案请求（RFP）和计费工时已被淘汰的世界。更换供应商就像点击一下鼠标那样简单，透明度也是绝对的。市场分裂为两部分：一部分是运营边际成本几乎为零、营业利润率高达 30-45% 的 AI 原生巨头，另一部分是因高成本而苦苦挣扎的老牌企业。人才格局发生了巨大变化——初级职位消失，需求集中在“信任经纪人”、“系统架构师”和“AI 治理者”上。视频最后向该行（在语境中被称为“Delaware”或类似名称）提出了一个存在主义问题：“有什么是你们能做而算法永远做不到的？”

  - [18:52:41 - 18:55:07] **Debriefing the Scenario: Customization at Scale**

    René emphasizes that this scenario was highly customized to the specific industry, something that would have required significant resources to produce manually. The "Nightmare Competitor" described in the exercise resonates with the scenario—an entity that reduces a "man-year" of SAP implementation work into a fraction of the time using AI tools.

    He points out the broader implication: AI allows for the mass customization of foresight work. Instead of one generic industry scenario, a firm can now generate specific scenario narratives for their supply chain department, their Asia-Pacific region, or their European division. This level of granularity was previously impossible due to budget and time constraints but is now feasible.

    René 强调，这个情景是针对特定行业高度定制的，如果手动制作需要大量资源。练习中描述的“噩梦竞争对手”与该情景产生了共鸣——即利用 AI 工具将原本需要“一人年”的 SAP 实施工作缩减为极短的时间。

    他指出了更广泛的含义：AI 使得前瞻工作的大规模定制成为可能。企业现在不再局限于一个通用的行业情景，而是可以为其供应链部门、亚太地区或欧洲分部生成特定的情景叙述。这种粒度水平以前受限于预算和时间是不可能实现的，但现在已变得可行。

  - [18:55:07 - 18:58:15] **Discussion: Trust, Accountability, and Hybrid Intelligence**

    René opens the floor for discussion regarding the threats and opportunities of using AI in strategy. He addresses comments about "hybrid intelligence" and accountability. He poses a provocative question about trust: In a partner-led firm, do partners trust a Managing Director (who answers to shareholders) more than they trust an AI? He draws a parallel to healthcare—patients might weigh the advice of a doctor against an AI tool based on the data provided.

    Professor Annapoornima adds that while AI can handle tasks, the human value-add lies in accountability and ethics. However, she questions whether companies genuinely prioritize these aspects over profit and performance, citing a news article about a cloud developer company that illustrates the tension between ethical considerations and the drive for revenue.

    René 开启了关于在战略中使用 AI 的威胁与机遇的讨论。他回应了关于“混合智能”和问责制的评论。他抛出了一个关于信任的挑衅性问题：在合伙制的公司中，合伙人是否比信任 AI 更信任（对股东负责的）董事总经理？他将其与医疗保健进行了类比——患者可能会根据提供的数据权衡医生与 AI 工具的建议。

    Annapoornima 教授补充说，虽然 AI 可以处理任务，但人类的增值在于问责制和道德。然而，她质疑公司是否真的将这些方面置于利润和绩效之上，并引用了一篇关于云开发公司的各类新闻文章，说明了道德考量与收入驱动之间的紧张关系。

  - [18:58:15 - 19:05:18] **Q&A: Red Oceans, Innovation Stagnation, and Real-Time Foresight**

    Addressing a question about whether AI creates "Red Oceans" (fierce competition) or "Blue Oceans," René expresses concern that AI might lead to "more of the same" rather than radical innovation. He cites the movie industry as an example where narratives feel recycled. He also touches on the use of Small Language Models (SLMs) for specific tasks, like restaurant ordering, to reduce hallucinations compared to broad LLMs.

    René summarizes his key takeaways for AI in foresight:

    1. **Perceiving:** AI enables real-time monitoring of tipping points rather than periodic scanning.

    2. **Prospecting:** It allows for real-time scenario planning and quick positioning against market changes.

    3. **Probing:** It enables rapid prototyping (e.g., coding an app mock-up in minutes) to test ideas immediately.

       He concludes with a warning: Students and professionals must not simply hit the "easy button." They must develop their own mental structures first and then use AI to iterate and test, otherwise, they risk relying on a system they don't understand.

    在回答关于 AI 是创造“红海”（激烈的竞争）还是“蓝海”的问题时，René 表达了担忧，认为 AI 可能会导致“千篇一律”，而不是激进的创新。他以电影行业为例，指出那里的叙事感觉像是回收利用的。他还提到了将小型语言模型（SLM）用于特定任务（如餐厅点餐），以减少相比通用 LLM 产生的幻觉。

    René 总结了他对前瞻中 AI 应用的关键要点：

    1. **感知：** AI 使得对临界点进行实时监控成为可能，而不是周期性的扫描。

    2. **勘探：** 它允许实时情景规划，并针对市场变化快速定位。

    3. **探索：** 它使得快速原型设计（例如在几分钟内编写一个应用程序模型）成为可能，以便立即测试想法。

       他最后发出警告：学生和专业人士不能简单地按下“简易按钮”。他们必须首先建立自己的心智结构，然后利用 AI 进行迭代和测试，否则他们将面临依赖一个自己并不理解的系统的风险。

  - [19:05:18 - 19:08:26] **Q&A: The Race to Catch Up**

    Professor Annapoornima remarks on the double burden firms now face: catching up on innovation itself, and simultaneously catching up on the *tools* (AI) used to innovate. She notes that the competition is likely to become "nasty."

    René agrees, noting that some investors and CEOs believe they can operate at "lightning speed" by using AI agents to bypass middle management entirely. While some companies reverse course after encountering hallucinations, the drive to automate high-level strategy and monitoring is strong, leading to a weird dichotomy where some firms are aggressively automating while others do nothing.

    Annapoornima 教授评论了企业现在面临的双重负担：既要追赶创新本身，又要同时追赶用于创新的*工具*（AI）。她指出，竞争可能会变得“残酷”。

    René 表示同意，并指出一些投资者和 CEO 相信他们可以通过使用 AI 代理完全绕过中层管理，以“闪电般的速度”运作。虽然有些公司在遇到幻觉问题后会改变方向，但自动化高层战略和监控的动力依然强劲，导致了一种奇怪的二分局面：一些公司正在积极自动化，而另一些公司则无动于衷。

  - [19:08:26 - 19:12:32] **Q&A: "Neurotic" vs. "Hypervigilant" Firms**

    Student Tan Yi Chun asks a question referencing René's benchmarking report about "neurotic firms"—those that over-invest in foresight relative to their needs. He asks if, given that AI lowers the cost of scanning, the definition of "neurotic" changes, and if every firm should now aim for maximum vigilance.

    René clarifies that he has rebranded "neurotic" to "hypervigilant" to be less stark. He explains that hypervigilant firms are those that "always live in the future" and try to compete in markets that don't exist yet, citing Elon Musk's many ventures (some successful, some not) as examples. He warns that AI might exacerbate this by making analysis so fast that firms detach from reality. Just because you can analyze a market instantly doesn't mean the market changes instantly. He advises that "Prospector" type firms should indeed build maximum foresight capabilities, but others should be careful not to detach from current customer behaviors.

    学生 Tan Yi Chun 引用 René 关于“神经质（Neurotic）公司”——即那些相对于自身需求在前瞻上过度投资的公司——的基准测试报告提出了一个问题。他问道，鉴于 AI 降低了扫描成本，“神经质”的定义是否发生了变化，是否每家公司现在都应该以此为目标，保持最大程度的警惕。

    René 澄清说，为了听起来不那么刺耳，他已将“神经质”重新命名为“过度警惕（Hypervigilant）”。他解释说，过度警惕的公司是那些“总是生活在未来”并试图在尚不存在的市场中竞争的公司，并引用埃隆·马斯克（Elon Musk）的众多冒险（有些成功，有些失败）作为例子。他警告说，AI 可能会通过使分析速度过快而加剧这种情况，导致公司脱离现实。仅仅因为你可以瞬间分析市场，并不意味着市场会瞬间改变。他建议，“探索者（Prospector）”类型的公司确实应该建立最大的前瞻能力，但其他公司应小心不要脱离当前的客户行为。

  - [19:12:32 - 19:19:57] **Q&A: The Future of Human Roles in IT and Consulting**

    Student Kang Tan, an IT industry veteran, expresses confusion and concern about the value of human roles. He observes that AI is replacing product managers and engineers—clients provide requests, and AI generates the code and architecture, with humans only tweaking a few lines. He references Kevin Kelly's book (specifically mentioning "2049" and "10,000 days," likely referring to *The Inevitable* or *5000 Days*) which suggests humans will become "shepherds" of AI. He asks: If clients can use AI to find data and trends themselves, what is the value add of a consultant?

    René acknowledges that coding is adopting AI fastest because code is verifiable (it works or it doesn't), whereas strategy is slower because the feedback loop is longer. However, he argues that humans are still needed for security, efficiency, and ensuring the code isn't hallucinated. More importantly, the human role shifts to "Ambassadorship"—understanding the customer, ensuring ethical alignment, and bridging the gap between AI output and human needs. He also mentions a backlash observed at Davos, where some stakeholders want to remove chatbots and AI to restore human connection.

    IT 行业资深人士 Kang Tan 表达了对人类角色价值的困惑和担忧。他观察到 AI 正在取代产品经理和工程师——客户提出需求，AI 生成代码和架构，人类只需微调几行。他引用了凯文·凯利（Kevin Kelly）的书（特别提到了“2049”和“10000 天”，可能指的是《必然》或《5000 天》），书中暗示人类将成为 AI 的“牧羊人”。他问道：如果客户可以自己使用 AI 查找数据和趋势，咨询顾问的增值价值在哪里？

    René 承认编码领域采用 AI 的速度最快，因为代码是可验证的（要么能跑，要么不能），而战略则较慢，因为反馈周期较长。然而，他认为人类在安全性、效率以及确保代码并非幻觉生成方面仍然是被需要的。更重要的是，人类的角色转变为“大使”——理解客户，确保道德一致性，并在 AI 输出与人类需求之间架起桥梁。他还提到了在达沃斯观察到的一种抵制情绪，一些利益相关者希望移除聊天机器人和 AI，以恢复人际联系。

  - [19:19:57 - 19:24:42] **Q&A: Security, Energy, and Primary Data**

    René briefly addresses chat comments about security (companies creating "walled gardens" because they can't upload data to public models) and the massive energy consumption of AI, which threatens to undo energy efficiency gains.

    Professor Annapoornima asks a final question about primary vs. secondary data. Since AI excels at processing secondary data, does primary data (human expertise) become a niche skill? René confirms that for innovation, AI is limited because LLMs are trained on historical, mainstream data ("more of the same"). Humans are still better at capturing the cutting edge. He reiterates that humans must stay intellectually engaged and not rely on the "easy button," or their careers will suffer. The session concludes with mutual thanks, and the class takes a break.

    René 简要回应了聊天中关于安全（公司建立“围墙花园”，因为无法将数据上传到公共模型）和 AI 巨大能源消耗的评论，这可能会抵消能源效率的收益。

    Annapoornima 教授提出了关于一手数据与二手数据的最后一个问题。既然 AI 擅长处理二手数据，那么一手数据（人类专业知识）是否会成为一项利基技能？René 确认，对于创新而言，AI 是有限的，因为 LLM 是基于历史、主流数据（“千篇一律”）训练的。人类在捕捉前沿信息方面仍然更胜一筹。他重申，人类必须保持智力投入，不能依赖“简易按钮”，否则职业生涯将受损。会议在相互致谢中结束，班级进入休息时间。

  - [19:40:16 - 19:43:04] **Debriefing the Guest Lecture and the AI Landscape**

    Professor Annapoornima welcomes the class back from the break and seeks immediate feedback on Professor René Rohrbeck's guest lecture. She asks if the content felt too abstract or high-level. A student comments that it was indeed somewhat abstract. Annapoornima clarifies that the intention wasn't to provide a hands-on tutorial for specific AI tools, but rather to map the broader landscape of how AI is currently permeating the field of foresight.

    She emphasizes that while AI is becoming the overarching force guiding activities like horizon scanning, scenario planning, and trend analysis, its adoption is uneven. For instance, the "Probing" phase relies less on AI because it involves direct investment in collaborators and venture capital—decisions driven by human stakeholders, even if those stakeholders use AI indirectly. She assures the class that specific tools for these activities will be covered in detail after the midterm break.

    Annapoornima 教授欢迎同学们休息归来，并征求大家对 René Rohrbeck 教授客座讲座的即时反馈。她询问内容是否感觉太抽象或层次太高。一名学生评论说确实有点抽象。Annapoornima 澄清说，讲座的目的并不是提供特定 AI 工具的实操教程，而是为了描绘 AI 目前如何渗透到前瞻领域的更广阔图景。

    她强调，虽然 AI 正成为指导地平线扫描、情景规划和趋势分析等活动的主导力量，但其采用并不均衡。例如，“探索（Probing）”阶段对 AI 的依赖较少，因为它涉及对合作者和风险投资的直接投资——这些决策由人类利益相关者驱动，即使这些人可能间接使用 AI。她向全班保证，期中假期后将详细讲解用于这些活动的具体工具。

  - [19:43:04 - 19:45:01] **Transition to Intelligence Frameworks**

    After a brief expression of frustration regarding the limitations of teaching via Zoom—specifically the inability to read students' faces or gauge their understanding—Annapoornima transitions back to the core lecture content (Slide 35 of Week 4). She recaps the process: once the mission and structure are established, the actual intelligence work begins—Searching, Filtering, Analyzing, Documenting, and Disseminating. She notes that while these steps sound straightforward, they are governed by critical frameworks that link intelligence directly to Knowledge Management (KM).

    在简短表达了对 Zoom 教学局限性（特别是无法看到学生面孔或判断他们的理解程度）的沮丧后，Annapoornima 转回核心讲座内容（第四周幻灯片第 35 页）。她回顾了流程：一旦确立了使命和结构，实际的情报工作就开始了——搜寻、过滤、分析、文档化和传播。她指出，虽然这些步骤听起来很直接，但它们受关键框架的管辖，这些框架将情报与知识管理（KM）直接联系起来。

  - [19:45:01 - 19:48:10] ** The Intelligence Awareness Matrix: Mine vs. Trawl**

    Annapoornima introduces a crucial 2x2 matrix to explain how organizations search for information. The X-axis represents **Intelligence Provision** (whether information is Internal or External), and the Y-axis represents **Intelligence Awareness** (whether you know what you know, or don't know what you know).

    She focuses first on the bottom-left quadrant: **Mine**. This occurs when an organization knows what it needs, and the expertise exists in-house. A firm with excellent Knowledge Management can simply "mine" this information. She uses NUS as an example: when she mentioned CO2 capture via gas hydrates, everyone immediately identified Professor Praveen Linga. This efficiency proves NUS has a strong awareness of its internal expertise.

    However, if a firm has internal expertise but lacks a good KM system, they fall into the **Trawl** quadrant. The knowledge resides in a human expert within the company, but no one knows who they are. The organization must "trawl" or skim through its own people to find the expert and make their implicit knowledge explicit (documenting it). Frequent trawling indicates a failure in Knowledge Management.

    Annapoornima 介绍了一个关键的 2x2 矩阵来解释组织如何搜索信息。X 轴代表**情报供应**（信息是内部的还是外部的），Y 轴代表**情报意识**（你知道你知道什么，还是你不知道你知道什么）。

    她首先关注左下象限：**挖掘（Mine）**。这发生在组织知道自己需要什么，且专业知识存在于内部时。拥有优秀知识管理的公司只需“挖掘”这些信息。她以新加坡国立大学（NUS）为例：当她提到通过气体水合物捕获二氧化碳时，每个人都立刻指出了 Praveen Linga 教授。这种效率证明 NUS 对其内部专业知识有很强的意识。

    然而，如果一家公司拥有内部专业知识但缺乏良好的知识管理系统，它们就会落入**搜寻（Trawl）**象限。知识存在于公司内部的某位专家身上，但没人知道是谁。组织必须在内部人员中“搜寻”或浏览，以找到该专家并将其隐性知识显性化（文档化）。频繁的搜寻表明知识管理存在失误。

  - [19:48:10 - 19:50:51] **The Intelligence Awareness Matrix: Scan vs. Target**

    Moving to the right side of the matrix (External Information), Annapoornima explains **Scanning**. This happens when knowledge is external, and the firm doesn't know exactly what it's looking for. This is unconditional searching for cutting-edge, embryonic, or weak signals to stay abreast of developments.

    Conversely, if the expertise is external but the firm *knows* exactly what it needs and who has it, this is **Targeting** (or Monitoring). For example, if you want to know about AI in education, you specifically target and monitor Georgia Tech.

    The ideal cycle for an innovative firm is to **Scan** for weak signals, identify valuable ones, turn them into **Targets**, and eventually acquire that knowledge to bring it in-house. Once internal, the firm must document it (Knowledge Management) so they can **Mine** it in the future, rather than having to **Trawl** for it again.

    转到矩阵的右侧（外部信息），Annapoornima 解释了**扫描（Scanning）**。这发生在知识位于外部，且公司不知道确切在寻找什么时。这是对前沿、萌芽或微弱信号的无条件搜索，以保持与发展同步。

    相反，如果专业知识在外部，但公司*确切知道*自己需要什么以及谁拥有它，这就是**定位（Targeting）**（或监控）。例如，如果你想了解教育中的 AI，你会专门定位并监控佐治亚理工学院。

    对于创新型公司来说，理想的循环是**扫描**微弱信号，识别有价值的信号，将其转化为**定位**目标，最终获取该知识并将其引入内部。一旦进入内部，公司必须将其文档化（知识管理），以便将来可以**挖掘**，而不是不得不再次**搜寻**。

  - [19:50:51 - 19:56:36] **Class Discussion: Real-world Applications of Scanning and Targeting**

    Annapoornima asks the class which activities their organizations perform most. Student **How Han Hong (Aaron)** shares that his consultancy firm focuses on **Scanning** for cybersecurity threats. Once a specific threat (like data governance) is identified, they **Target** specialized suppliers. Ultimately, they aim to acquire these suppliers to bring the capability in-house. Annapoornima validates this but warns that the value of acquisition depends on integration; research shows that if key experts leave after acquisition, the firm is forced to "Trawl" again, wasting the value of the original scan.

    Student **Meredith (ESG)** shares that her large organization uses **Targeting** for specific "microcosms" of technology they are already aware of, while simultaneously **Scanning** for unknown upcoming trends. Internally, they have a strong **Mining** culture: every meeting requires a "Call Report" logged in their system. Before engaging a company, they search these logs to see previous interactions. Annapoornima praises this, recounting a counter-example where a former student struggled to write a proposal because her firm lacked records of previous projects with the same client, forcing them to start from scratch.

    Annapoornima 询问班级他们的组织最常执行哪些活动。学生 **How Han Hong (Aaron)** 分享说，他的咨询公司专注于**扫描**网络安全威胁。一旦识别出特定威胁（如数据治理），他们就会**定位**专业供应商。最终，他们的目标是收购这些供应商以将能力引入内部。Annapoornima 肯定了这一点，但警告说收购的价值取决于整合；研究表明，如果关键专家在收购后离职，公司将被迫再次“搜寻”，从而浪费了最初扫描的价值。

    学生 **Meredith (ESG)** 分享说，她所在的大型组织针对他们已知的特定技术“微观世界”使用**定位**，同时**扫描**未知的即将到来的趋势。在内部，他们有很强的**挖掘**文化：每次会议都需要在系统中记录“通话报告”。在接触一家公司之前，他们会搜索这些日志以查看以前的互动。Annapoornima 对此表示赞赏，并讲述了一个反面教材：以前的一位学生在撰写提案时遇到了困难，因为她的公司缺乏与同一客户以前项目的记录，迫使他们从头开始。

  - [19:56:36 - 20:02:15] **Passive vs. Active Scanning and Monitoring**

    The Professor discusses the "Information Needs Template." If done well, it reduces the burden of random scanning. She points out that senior management often travels for specific agendas (e.g., signing an MOU) but picks up market signals incidentally.

    Student **Eugene** asks for clarification: "Isn't traveling and obtaining information part of scanning?" Annapoornima clarifies the distinction between **Passive** and **Active**:

    - **Passive Scanning:** Picking up signals incidentally while doing something else (e.g., a President visiting a partner university).

    - **Active Scanning:** Deliberately sending "Pathfinders" or attending a conference specifically to harvest latest research.

    - **Passive Monitoring:** Keeping a "watch out" on a company that isn't yet ripe for investment but could become a disruptor.

    - **Active Monitoring:** Closely tracking a company you have invested in.

      She notes that effective intelligence work involves moving items from Passive Scanning to Passive Monitoring to ensure they don't "bite you in the back."

    教授讨论了“信息需求模板”。如果做得好，它可以减轻随机扫描的负担。她指出，高级管理层经常因特定议程（例如签署谅解备忘录）出差，但会顺便收集市场信号。

    学生 **Eugene** 要求澄清：“出差和获取信息不就是扫描的一部分吗？”Annapoornima 阐明了**被动**与**主动**的区别：

    - **被动扫描：** 在做其他事情时顺便收集信号（例如校长访问合作大学）。

    - **主动扫描：**以此为目的特意派遣“探路者”或参加会议以收集最新研究成果。

    - **被动监控：** 对一家尚不成熟值得投资但可能成为颠覆者的公司保持“关注”。

    - **主动监控：** 密切跟踪你已经投资的公司。

      她指出，有效的情报工作涉及将项目从被动扫描转移到被动监控，以确保它们不会“反咬一口”。

  - [20:02:15 - 20:05:48] **Assignment Clarification: The Lichtenthaler Article**

    Annapoornima pauses to clarify the compulsory logbook assignment involving the article by **Lichtenthaler** (referred to phonetically as "Left Tentaler" in the raw audio, corrected based on context). She instructs students to ignore the general theory in the beginning of the paper and focus strictly on the sections detailing **Scanning and Monitoring**.

    The key takeaway for the logbook is to analyze the "Human Element": What kind of knowledge base should a scanner have? What are the pitfalls if their scope is too narrow? The paper details the communication structures and personnel requirements for these activities.

    Annapoornima 暂停了一下，以澄清涉及 **Lichtenthaler** 文章的强制性日志作业。她指示学生忽略论文开头的一般理论，严格关注详述**扫描和监控**的部分。

    日志的关键要点是分析“人的因素”：扫描人员应该具备什么样的知识库？如果他们的视野太窄会有什么陷阱？该论文详细介绍了这些活动的沟通结构和人员要求。

  - [20:05:48 - 20:11:09] **Sources of Information and Databases**

    Returning to the framework, Annapoornima discusses where to search for information.  She lists standard sources like journals, reports, and statistics (e.g., OECD), but highlights **Patents** and **Bibliometrics** (publications) as particularly rich sources.

    She provides specific recommendations for databases available via the NUS library:

    - **Frost & Sullivan** and **LexisNexis**: Excellent for market reports, benchmarking, and competitive intelligence (e.g., identifying the top 10 drone manufacturers and their metrics).

    - **PatSnap**: The primary tool for patent data (replacing Questel/Orbit for general students).

    - **Web of Science** and **Scopus**: The go-to databases for publication data.

      She emphasizes that "secondary data" like reports can be analyzed quickly with AI, but primary data requires more effort.

    回到框架，Annapoornima 讨论了在哪里搜索信息。她列举了期刊、报告和统计数据（如 OECD）等标准来源，但强调**专利**和**文献计量学**（出版物）是特别丰富的信息源。

    她推荐了可通过新加坡国立大学图书馆访问的具体数据库：

    - **Frost & Sullivan** 和 **LexisNexis**：非常适合市场报告、基准测试和竞争情报（例如识别前 10 名无人机制造商及其指标）。

    - **PatSnap（智慧芽）**：专利数据的主要工具（针对普通学生替代 Questel/Orbit）。

    - **Web of Science** 和 **Scopus**：出版物数据的首选数据库。

      她强调，像报告这样的“二手数据”可以用 AI 快速分析，但一手数据需要更多的努力。

  - [20:11:09 - 20:17:35] **Matching Information Sources to the Technology S-Curve**

    Annapoornima introduces the **Technology S-Curve** to explain that the *type* of information you search for depends on the technology's maturity.

    - **Embryonic Stage (Start of S-Curve):** Progress is slow. You cannot rely on "White Information" (published reports/patents) because it doesn't exist yet. You must use **Gray Information** (talking to experts/Delphi method) or **Black Information** (informal/restricted). You rely on publications and primary data here.

    - **Mature Stage (Top of S-Curve):** The technology is saturated. Here, you use **White Information**—patents, product specs, and market reports are abundant.

      She warns that looking for patents at the embryonic stage is futile, just as looking for breakthrough scientific publications for a fully mature technology is a waste of time.

    Annapoornima 引入**技术 S 曲线**来解释你搜索的信息*类型*取决于技术的成熟度。

    - **萌芽阶段（S 曲线的起点）：** 进展缓慢。你不能依赖“白色信息”（已发布的报告/专利），因为它还不存在。你必须使用**灰色信息**（与专家交谈/德尔菲法）或**黑色信息**（非正式/受限）。在这里你依赖出版物和一手数据。

    - **成熟阶段（S 曲线的顶部）：** 技术已经饱和。在这里，你使用**白色信息**——专利、产品规格和市场报告非常丰富。

      她警告说，在萌芽阶段寻找专利是徒劳的，就像为完全成熟的技术寻找突破性的科学出版物是在浪费时间一样。

  - [20:17:35 - 20:23:44] **Overview of Tools and the Mortara Article**

    The Professor briefly addresses the "Tools" component of the framework. Acknowledging that there are too many tools to cover in depth (both qualitative and quantitative), she adopts a blended learning approach. She will provide videos for basic skills like Excel trend curve fitting and will focus on the most important tools in class.

    She directs students back to the **Mortara et al.** article (Week 4 reading) covering UK technology-based companies. This paper validates the theoretical framework (Mine/Trawl/Scan/Target) by showing its application in the real world. She encourages students to read it to see which approaches—Top-down vs. Bottom-up—are actually used by firms.

    教授简要介绍了框架中的“工具”部分。她承认工具太多，无法深入涵盖所有工具（包括定性和定量），因此她采用了混合学习方法。她将提供有关 Excel 趋势曲线拟合等基本技能的视频，并将在课堂上重点介绍最重要的工具。

    她引导学生回顾 **Mortara 等人**的文章（第四周阅读材料），该文章涵盖了英国的技术型公司。这篇论文通过展示其在现实世界中的应用，验证了理论框架（挖掘/搜寻/扫描/定位）。她鼓励学生阅读该文章，以了解公司实际使用了哪些方法——自上而下还是自下而上。

  - [20:23:44 - 20:28:46] **Introduction to Knowledge Management (KM)**

    Annapoornima transitions to the Week 5 & 7 slides to introduce **Knowledge Management**. She asks the class to define it.

    - **Meredith** defines it as organizing knowledge to be accessible (Knowledge Capture).

    - **Kang Tan** broadens it to collection, analysis, use, and refresh.

    - **Eugene** describes it as the entire process of capturing someone's experience, putting it into words, and sharing it periodically so it isn't forgotten.

      Annapoornima appreciates these definitions but insists on defining "Knowledge" itself first, distinguishing it from Data and Information.

    Annapoornima 转到第五周和第七周的幻灯片，介绍**知识管理**。她请全班给它下个定义。

    - **Meredith** 将其定义为组织知识以便于访问（知识捕获）。

    - **Kang Tan** 将其扩展为收集、分析、使用和更新。

    - **Eugene** 将其描述为捕获某人经验、将其转化为文字并定期分享以防被遗忘的整个过程。

      Annapoornima 赞赏这些定义，但坚持首先定义“知识”本身，将其与数据和信息区分开来。

  - [20:28:46 - 20:33:09] **The Hierarchy: Data, Information, and Knowledge**

    Annapoornima breaks down the hierarchy:

    1. **Data:** Observations brought to attention (e.g., The raw temperature reading in her room).

    2. **Information:** Meaning derived from data by comparing it over time/context (e.g., Plotting the temperature to see if it is rising or stable).

    3. **Knowledge:** **A belief in a cause-and-effect relationship.**

       She uses a personal anecdote to illustrate: She records the room temperature (Data). She notices it rising (Information). She knows from experience that if it gets too hot, she will have a panic attack (Knowledge/Cause-and-Effect). Knowledge is simply the understanding that "X causes Y."

    Annapoornima 分解了这个层级结构：

    1. **数据：**引起注意的观察结果（例如，她房间里的原始温度读数）。

    2. **信息：** 通过随时间/背景比较数据得出的含义（例如，绘制温度图以查看它是上升还是稳定）。

    3. **知识：** **对因果关系的信念。**

       她用一个个人轶事来说明：她记录房间温度（数据）。她注意到温度在上升（信息）。她从经验中知道，如果太热，她会恐慌发作（知识/因果关系）。知识仅仅是对“X 导致 Y”的理解。

  - [20:33:09 - 20:36:37] **Sense-Making**

    The process of moving from Information to Knowledge is called **Sense-Making**. Karishma explains her understanding based on a startup analyzing AI trends to understand impacts on clients. Annapoornima defines Sense-Making formally as "perceiving events, looking for similarities/differences with the past, and forming expectations."

    She uses the analogy of a child and a hot stove. A child touches a cold stove (past event = safe). The child touches a hot stove (current event = pain). The child engages in sense-making to distinguish the context (Burner On vs. Burner Off) and establishes the cause-and-effect relationship (Knowledge). Organizations do the same when facing disruption—they compare current threats to past survival to decide how to act.

    从信息到知识的过程称为**意义建构（Sense-Making）**。Karishma 基于一家初创公司分析 AI 趋势以了解对客户影响的案例，解释了她的理解。Annapoornima 将意义建构正式定义为“感知事件，寻找与过去的异同，并形成期望”。

    她用了孩子和热炉子的类比。孩子摸了一个冷炉子（过去事件 = 安全）。孩子摸了一个热炉子（当前事件 = 疼痛）。孩子进行意义建构以区分背景（炉头开 vs. 炉头关），并建立因果关系（知识）。组织在面临颠覆时也会做同样的事情——他们将当前的威胁与过去的生存经历进行比较，以决定如何行动。

  - [20:41:11 - 20:41:58] **Sense-Making and Interpretive Frameworks**

    Professor Annapoornima elaborates on the cognitive process of "Sense-Making." She explains that human survival and decision-making depend on comparing current events with past experiences to identify cause-and-effect relationships. For example, when observing AI disrupting industries, an organization engages in sense-making by asking, "Should we adopt this?" They look back at past technological shifts: "In the past, when we adopted early, we succeeded; those who didn't failed." This historical correlation informs the current decision.

    She introduces the concept of **Interpretive Frameworks**—existing sets of beliefs about causal relationships accumulated over time. For individuals, these reside in the brain; for organizations, they reside in Knowledge Management systems or the collective minds of employees (since much tacit knowledge cannot be easily documented). When a new event occurs, the organization taps into these frameworks to derive intelligence and convert data into information and knowledge.

    Annapoornima 教授详细阐述了“意义建构（Sense-Making）”的认知过程。她解释说，人类的生存和决策依赖于将当前事件与过去的经验进行比较，以识别因果关系。例如，当观察到 AI 颠覆各行各业时，组织会进行意义建构，通过询问“我们要采用这个吗？”来进行思考。他们回顾过去的技术变革：“过去，当我们尽早采用时，我们成功了；那些没有采用的人失败了。”这种历史相关性为当前的决策提供了依据。

    她介绍了**解释框架（Interpretive Frameworks）**的概念——即随着时间积累的关于因果关系的既有信念集。对于个人而言，这些框架存在于大脑中；对于组织而言，它们存在于知识管理系统或员工的集体思维中（因为许多隐性知识难以轻易文档化）。当新事件发生时，组织会利用这些框架来获取情报，并将数据转化为信息和知识。

  - [20:41:58 - 20:42:04] **The Strategic Value of a Diverse Workforce**

    The Professor connects the concept of Interpretive Frameworks to the importance of diversity. She argues that organizations need a diverse workforce because each individual carries a unique interpretive framework shaped by their specific life experiences—where they grew up, studied, and worked. Her own framework, shaped by growing up in India and studying in the US, differs from her colleagues'. When diverse people come together, they bring different lenses for sense-making, allowing new ideas to emerge and broadening the organization's understanding of cause-and-effect relationships. This makes the organization more knowledgeable and capable.

    教授将解释框架的概念与多样性的重要性联系起来。她认为组织需要多元化的员工队伍，因为每个人都通过其特定的生活经历——成长、求学和工作的地方——形成了独特的解释框架。她自己因在印度成长和在美国求学而形成的框架，就与她的同事不同。当不同的人聚在一起时，他们为意义建构带来了不同的视角，从而激发新想法的出现，并拓宽组织对因果关系的理解。这使得组织更加知识渊博，能力更强。

  - [20:42:04 - 20:42:58] **Distinguishing Intelligence from Knowledge**

    Annapoornima clarifies the subtle distinction between Intelligence and Knowledge based on the level of personalization.

    - **Intelligence:** When you encounter a completely new event that doesn't match any past experience, you gather data and unrelated information to make sense of it. This process is **impersonal** because you lack direct experience.

    - **Knowledge:** Once that intelligence is validated through experience and becomes a firm belief in a cause-and-effect relationship, it becomes **personal**.

      Essentially, intelligence is the raw material of understanding new environments, while knowledge is the solidified, experienced belief that guides action.

    Annapoornima 根据个性化程度澄清了情报与知识之间的细微区别。

    - **情报（Intelligence）：** 当你遇到一个与过去任何经验都不匹配的全新事件时，你会收集数据和不相关的信息来理解它。这个过程是**非个性化（Impersonal）**的，因为你缺乏直接经验。

    - **知识（Knowledge）：** 一旦该情报通过经验得到验证，并成为对因果关系的坚定信念，它就变成了**个性化（Personal）**的。

      本质上，情报是理解新环境的原材料，而知识是指导行动的、经过固化的经验信念。

  - [20:42:58 - 20:45:28] **Defining Organizational Knowledge: The Tiger Analogy**

    The Professor provides a formal definition of **Organizational Knowledge**: "A shared belief in a cause-and-effect relationship that is accepted as valid and acted upon by enough people in an organization to form a critical mass for taking action." She emphasizes that if only the boss believes "A causes B" (e.g., "Adopting AI leads to competitive advantage"), it remains personal knowledge. It only becomes organizational knowledge when the workforce accepts it and acts on it.

    To illustrate, she shares a vivid analogy from a Copenhagen professor. Imagine a message is broadcast to the classroom: "An animal with orange and black stripes is entering."

    - **Scenario A:** The students interpret this as "A Tiger is coming -> Run for your life!" (Shared cause-and-effect). They escape and survive.

    - **Scenario B:** The students interpret this as "A large cat is entering -> No big deal, we are in safe Singapore." They stay put. If it turns out to be a real tiger, the organization fails (they get eaten).

      This demonstrates that organizational knowledge is not just about having information, but about the *shared interpretation* and the resulting *collective action*.

    教授提供了**组织知识**的正式定义：“一种对因果关系的共同信念，该信念被组织中足够多的人接受为有效并付诸行动，从而形成采取行动的临界质量。”她强调，如果只有老板相信“A 导致 B”（例如，“采用 AI 带来竞争优势”），那它仍然只是个人知识。只有当员工接受并据此行动时，它才成为组织知识。

    为了说明这一点，她分享了一位哥本哈根教授的生动类比。想象一下，教室里广播了一条消息：“一种有橙色和黑色条纹的动物正在进入。”

    - **情景 A：** 学生将其解读为“老虎来了 -> 赶紧逃命！”（共同的因果关系）。他们逃跑并幸存下来。

    - **情景 B：** 学生将其解读为“一只大猫进来了 -> 没什么大不了的，我们在安全的各种加坡。”他们原地不动。如果结果是一只真正的老虎，组织就失败了（他们被吃掉了）。

      这表明，组织知识不仅仅是拥有信息，更在于*共同的解释*以及随之而来的*集体行动*。

  - [20:45:28 - 20:50:52] **Organizational Learning: Three Types of Changes**

    Annapoornima defines **Organizational Learning** as a change in the cause-and-effect relationship over time. She categorizes this learning into three types:

    1. **Change in the Rule (A ≠ B anymore):**
       - *Belief:* "Chinese New Year (A) -> High Inventory Sales (B)."
       - *Learning:* Sales are actually driven by Consumer Mood/Security (X). If people fear AI will take their jobs, they save money despite the festival. The rule shifts from "Festival -> Sales" to "Security -> Sales."
    2. **Change in the Degree of Belief (A -> B is weaker/stronger):**
       - *Belief:* "Winter (A) -> Sales of Winter Clothes (B)."
       - *Learning:* This holds true for women (fashion-driven), but less so for men (practical/temperature-driven). The organization learns that the relationship's strength varies by demographic.
    3. **Change in the Condition (A -> B only if C):**
       - *Belief:* "Competitor lowers price (A) -> Price War (B)."
       - *Learning:* Sometimes a price drop is just to clear overstocked inventory. If you misinterpret an inventory clearance as a price war and slash your own prices, you destroy your margins. The rule "Price Drop -> Retaliate" is only valid under the condition that it is an actual aggressive move, not just housekeeping.

    Annapoornima 将**组织学习**定义为随时间推移因果关系的变化。她将这种学习分为三类：

    1. **规则的改变（A 不再导致 B）：**
       - *信念：* “农历新年（A） -> 高库存销售（B）。”
       - *学习：* 销售实际上是由消费者情绪/安全感（X）驱动的。如果人们担心 AI 会夺走他们的工作，即使过节他们也会存钱。规则从“节日 -> 销售”转变为“安全感 -> 销售”。
    2. **信念程度的改变（A -> B 变弱/变强）：**
       - *信念：* “冬天（A） -> 冬装销售（B）。”
       - *学习：* 这对女性（时尚驱动）适用，但对男性（实用/温度驱动）适用性较差。组织了解到该关系的强度因人群而异。
    3. **条件的改变（仅当 C 时，A -> B）：**
       - *信念：* “竞争对手降价（A） -> 价格战（B）。”
       - *学习：* 有时降价只是为了清理积压的库存。如果你将清理库存误读为价格战并大幅削减自己的价格，你就会破坏自己的利润率。规则“降价 -> 反击”仅在它是真正的攻击性举动而非仅仅是清理门户的条件下才有效。

  - [20:50:52 - 20:53:08] **Conclusion and Administrative Announcements**

    The Professor concludes the lecture by reiterating that viewing knowledge as a simple "cause-and-effect" relationship makes it much easier to manage than abstract definitions. She decides to stop there to avoid Zoom fatigue.

    She outlines the schedule for the upcoming weeks:

    - **Next Week:** No class (Chinese New Year).
    - **Following Week:** No class (Midterm Break).
    - **Next Meeting:** March 4th (First week of March).

    She reminds students to use the long break to work on the compulsory **Lichtenthaler logbook** entry regarding Scanning and Monitoring. She also advises them to start forming their groups and thinking about their group projects. She closes by wishing everyone a safe and happy Chinese New Year celebration.

    教授在讲座结束时重申，将知识视为简单的“因果”关系，比抽象的定义更容易管理。为了避免大家的 Zoom 疲劳，她决定就此停下。

    她概述了未来几周的安排：

    - **下周：** 无课（农历新年）。
    - **下下周：** 无课（期中假期）。
    - **下次见面：** 3 月 4 日（3 月的第一周）。

    她提醒学生利用长假完成关于扫描和监控的强制性 **Lichtenthaler 日志**条目。她还建议大家开始组队并思考他们的小组项目。最后，她祝愿大家度过一个安全、快乐的农历新年。

# Discussion
## Discussion Week 4
  During my time as an Algorithm Engineer, our Technology Intelligence (TI) activities mainly focused on **Targeting and Scanning**. This includes many kinds of SOTA architectures we can provide toour customers, like recent LLM models, Stable Diffusion and acceleration techniques (e.g., quantization, speculative decoding).

  **How we captured impact:**
  We focused on **technical performance metrics** firstly,instead of direct economic valuation in the short term. For achieving this, We used strict technical benchmarks. For example, when porting a PyTorch model to our inference framework, the KPIs were **inference latency** (ms), **throughput** (tokens/sec), and **accuracy retention** (ensuring loss < 1% after quantization). In the long-term, the value was actually valued by the **enablement of hardware ecosystems**. By successfully optimizing these models, we ensured our hardware remained competitive against our competitors.

  **Who conducted the assessment:**
  We have a team, which is normally 2-3 people, specifically investigating new technologies, and validated by out project leaders or higher level discussion meetings. So it's both a bottom-up and top-down process.

  **Suggestions for Improvement:**
  While our technical KPIs were precise, we lacked a direct link to **economic KPIs** during the R&D phase. Sometimes we need to go to customers' site for further debugging of their issues, and it could be a better opportunity for understanding their pain points, but it's not very frequently.
  An improvement would be talk and hear directly from customers, This would help engineering teams better visualize the business value of the intelligence activity beyond just "beating the benchmark."

***

# Syllabus
## Course Description
  Successful R&D engineers and managers should have the foresight to anticipate and drive technological changes and convert them into strategic assets to organizations. This course will equip students with technology forecasting, intelligence and foresighting skills, make use of the foresight to generate strategic intellectual assets and realize value from them to succeed in competitive environment. Effective collection and transformation of information into intelligence requires awareness of enterprise niches and alternatives, as well as the search and analytical skills of data and information. The course will emphasize these skills and impart a thorough understanding business & technology related strategic frameworks.
## Welcome to the course!
  Welcome to MT5010!

  I am Annapoornima Subramanian, lecturer for MT5010 for this semester.

  We all know that organizations need to develop insights into future alternatives and be relevant in order to enjoy sustained competitive advantage. Doing so is more critical for R&D intensive organizations as firms in high-technology industries are constantly threatened with technological discontinuities. Therefore, this module aims to equip students with strategic insights and analytical skills of technology forecasting & intelligence that are essential for high-tech companies to survive in a transient and competitive environment. Effective technological intelligence and forecasting requires a comprehensive awareness of enterprise niches and alternatives, analytical skills of data/information, knowledge management and considerations to organizational structures. Hence, this module covers range of topics including technology intelligence (a) mission (b) structure (c) processes, (d) management, and (e) tools.  Thus, apart from introducing the theory and practice of technology forecasting & intelligence, the module will provide hands-on training on technology intelligence and forecasting tools.
## Grading Components & Details
  The grading requirement involves both individual and group work. Individual work includes class participation, and a logbook submission. Group work includes a group project (either of a company of your choice or Straumann/NRP cases provided in Canvas).

  The breakdown of grading components is as follows

  Grading

  Individual Component (60%)

  Class Participation 30%
  Logbook  (26 April, 9pm) 30%
  Group Component (40%)
  Group Project or Straumann case or Singapore's NRP (15 April) 40%                                     
  Description

  Individual Component

  Class Participation (30% grade): Students are expected to analyze the readings and cases and contribute to class discussion. You are graded on quality rather than quantity. I will be inviting many guest lecturers for this module. Asking interesting questions during the guest lectures is a way to improve your class participation score.

  Logbook (30% grade): Throughout the semester, I will assign articles for discussion in each class and facilitate group activities. You are required to maintain a logbook that documents the discussion components from each session. Students who have taken MT5007 may already be familiar with this requirement; for those who haven't, I will provide a detailed briefing during the first lecture.

  Your logbook should focus on capturing the key discussion points from each class and connecting these insights to real-world applications. You need to cover a maximum of five topics in your logbook. The submission deadline is April 26, 2026.

  Group Component

  Group Project (40% grade)  Students are expected to form groups by themselves. Groups are expected to make a presentation and it can take one of the following two forms. Please note that there is no need to submit report. Just presentation is enough and slides are to be submitted to Canvas. Each group will have to make a presentation for 15-18 mins. This will be followed by Q&A for 2 mins.

  Technology Intelligence practices in your organization/If you were to initiate Technology Intelligence activities in your organization, how would you go about structuring and executing them.
  Presentation on Technological Intelligence Activities in a SME called Straumann. This case is published in a book. Groups need to understand the TI journey of Straumann and present their critical analysis of the same.
  Presentation on the Strategic foresight activities of Singapore’s National Robotics Programme (NRP). This case is published in a book. Groups need to understand the journey of Strategic Foresight Journey of NRP Singapore and present their critical analysis of the same.

## WEEK 8 Technology Intelligence & Foresighting Methods
  - In the second half of the module, we will focus on technology intelligence methods such as Delphi Method, Trend Analysis, S-Curve Analysis, Bibliometric Analysis, Roadmapping, Technology Radar. For many of these methods, I have experts in the respective methodology giving guest lecture.
  - Please go through Schmidt’s paper on Delphi method. You need not go through the details of the research, but just how they executed the Delphi method across different rounds. Just focus on that part.
  - In this week, I will be covering the rest of knowledge management and touch upon Delphi method. Please prepare yourself with the below reading material. Also, go through the video on Kendall's coefficient of concordance in Excel.
  - Things this year are going to be very different. Most of the videos that I recorded for methods will outline the background information using Excel. I wanted to resort to software that most of you have access to without a subscription. That is why I used Excel or other open-source software. However, with the advent of GenAI, everything is different this year. Most of the methods could be executed with simple prompts. I tried them on Claude, and it works. However, unless you give a super-specific prompt, Claude's first few answers are always wrong. So please be mindful of that. Further, the optimization method used by GenAI is quite different from that of Excel packages. So the answers are a bit different. Be mindful of those. I will let you know more in class. However, the blessing is that things have become very simple (though not sure if it's for the good 😊). I don’t have to deal with methods in an elaborate way, as a simple command in GenAI can execute all the methods (except for bibliometric analysis, as far as I know).
  - **Learning Outcomes** By the end of this week, you will be able to:
    - Have a good understanding of Delphi method and Kendall's W coefficient on inter-rater reliability

## WEEK 11 Technology Intelligence & Foresighting Methods
  In the second half of the module, we will focus on technology intelligence methods such as Delphi Method, Trend Analysis, S-Curve Analysis, Bibliometric Analysis, Roadmapping, Technology Radar. For many of these methods, I have experts in the respective methodology giving guest lecture. In Week 10, I will be covering Bibliometric analysis using software such as VOSViewer, Pajek and Bibexcel.

  Learning Outcomes
  By the end of this week, you will be able to:

  Have a good understanding of conducting bibliometric analysis using software such as VOSViewer, Pajek and Bibexcel.

## WEEK 12 Technology Intelligence & Foresighting Methods
  In the second half of the module, we will focus on technology intelligence methods such as Delphi Method, Trend Analysis, S-Curve Analysis, Bibliometric Analysis, Roadmapping, Technology Radar. For many of these methods, I have experts in the respective methodology giving guest lecture. In Week 11, I will be covering Scenario Planning, and Foresight Maturity Model.

  Learning Outcomes
  By the end of this week, you will be able to:

   Have a good understanding of methods such as Scenario Planning, and also understand about Foresight Maturity Model.
